1. Introduction to Spring Framework 
Spring is a powerful, lightweight framework used for building Java applications, especially 
enterprise-level apps. It helps to develop loosely coupled applications through Dependency 
Injection and Aspect-Oriented Programming. 
Key Features: 
 Lightweight and fast 
 Supports Dependency Injection (DI) 
 Modular architecture 
 Integrates well with other technologies (Hibernate, JPA, Struts, etc.) 
 Offers tools like Spring Boot, Spring Data, and Spring Security. 
Java Learning Categories 
1. Java Language – Core Java concepts 
2. Java Technologies – JDBC, Servlets, JSP, JSTL, EJB, JMS, etc. 
3. Frameworks – Hibernate, Spring, Spring Boot, Microservices, REST APIs 
Framework = Abstraction layer built on existing technologies (provides boilerplate code 
generation) 
Framework Types 
• Web Application Framework: Struts, Spring MVC, JSF, Web Work 
• ORM Framework: Hibernate, Top Link, iBatis 
• Application Framework: Spring 
• Distributed App Framework: RESTful services, SOAP, Jersey, Rest Easy. 
Invasive vs Non-Invasive Frameworks 
Invasive Framework: - Developer must extend/implement  
framework classes - Tightly coupled, less portable - Examples: Servlet, Struts 
Non-Invasive Framework: - No extension/implementation required - Loosely coupled, highly portable - Examples: Spring, Hibernate 
A significant drawback to building applications 
with technologies like JDBC and plain Java classes 
is the requirement to write all the code from the 
ground up. This involves manually developing 
components such as POJO (Plain Old Java Object) 
classes and their corresponding parameters. 
The Spring Framework addresses this drawback 
by providing additional libraries that eliminate 
the need to write so much boilerplate code. 
Framework = Abstraction layer built on existing technologies 
(provides boilerplate code generation) 
EXP: 
Hibernate -----> based on configuration details supplied, it will create JDBC environment 
Spring -----> based on configuration details supplied, it will create an object and maintains the 
object and performs dependency injection. 
Different types of Framework to build application: 
a. Web application based framework 
b. ORM Framework 
c. Application Framework 
d. BigData Framework 
e. Distrubuted Application Development framework.

Evolution of spring 
• 1995 – Applets (limited to gaming) 
• 1996 – JavaBeans (only local clients) 
• 1998 – EJB – for distributed apps (complex, server-dependent) 
• 2002/03 – Spring Framework by Rod Johnson (lightweight, flexible). 
Is Spring an alternative to EJB, Struts, Hibernate, or JEE? 
Answer: No. Spring is not a direct alternative to these technologies. Instead, it is a comprehensive 
framework that integrates, simplifies, and offers alternatives to parts of EJB, Struts, Hibernate, and 
JEE. 
Spring vs EJB (Enterprise JavaBeans) 
Aspect EJB Spring 
Type Component-based 
framework from JEE 
Lightweight, modular 
application framework 
Purpose Used for distributed, 
transactional, secure 
apps 
Same purpose, but more 
flexible and testable 
Web Services Web services can 
replace some EJB use 
cases 
Spring supports web 
services too 
Verdict  Spring provides 
alternatives to EJB 
features like transaction 
management, 
dependency injection, 
and AOP 
Spring vs Struts 
Aspect Struts Spring (Spring MVC) 
Type Web MVC Framework General-purpose + Web 
MVC (Spring MVC) 
Scope Only for web apps Can build web, desktop, 
microservices, etc. 
Verdict  Spring MVC is a 
replacement/alternative to 
Struts, offering better 
integration and modularity. 
Spring vs Hibernate 
Aspect Hibernate Spring 
Type ORM framework Full-stack framework with 
ORM module 
Purpose Maps Java objects to DB 
tables 
Provides abstraction for 
ORM 
Example SessionFactory, Criteria 
API 
SpringORM, Spring Data 
JPA 
Verdict  Spring uses Hibernate 
internally and offers 
abstraction via Spring 
ORM and Spring Data 
JPA. 
Spring vs JEE (Jakarta EE) 
Aspect JEE (Java EE / Jakarta EE) Spring 
Type Specification/API standard Framework that 
implements & extends JEE 
features 
Features Servlet, JSP, JPA, JDBC, 
JMS, etc. 
Spring JDBC, Spring 
MVC, Spring JMS, etc. 
Verdict  Spring provides 
abstractions on top of JEE 
APIs, making development 
easier and more testable. 
Summary Points 
 - Spring is not a direct competitor to any single technology but offers easier alternatives and better integration. - Spring MVC vs Struts → Yes, Spring MVC is an alternative. - Spring ORM vs Hibernate → Not an alternative, but an abstraction. - Spring vs EJB → Spring simplifies and replaces EJB features like transactions and remoting. - Spring vs JEE → Spring builds on and simplifies JEE specs. - Examples: 
    • Spring JDBC → wraps JDBC API 
    • Spring MVC → wraps Servlet/JSP 
    • Spring Data JPA → wraps JPA 
Spring Framework – Key Advantages - All types of app development supported - Non-invasive programming model - Built-in middleware services (transactions, connection pooling) - Lightweight and easy to learn - Portable and modular 
Spring Core Module - Base module for all other Spring modules - Provides IoC Containers: 
  - BeanFactory (older) 
  - ApplicationContext (preferred, newer) - Responsibilities: 
  - Managing bean lifecycle 
  - Dependency management using DI and Lookup 
Spring Application Config Approaches 
1. XML-based configuration 
2. Annotation-driven configuration 
3. Java-based configuration 
4. Spring Boot (auto-configuration) 
Dependency Management Explained - Target Class: Uses another class (e.g., Flipkart, Student, Vehicle) - Dependent Class: Helper class (e.g., DTDC, Engine, CourseMaterial) 
Recommended Practical Reference 
Project Example Mentioned: IOCProj1 – Setter Injection 
Dependency Management:- 
It is the process of assigning dependent object to Target object by loading both the classes and by 
creating the objects for both the classes. 
 *The classes/objects, which uses the other class services, is called "Target class". 
 * The classes that acts like helper class to main/target class is called "Dependent class". 
  eg:: Target class => Flipkart, Vehicle, 
  Student, Mobile 
  Dependent class => DTDC , Engine , 
  Course Material, SIM 
  refer: IOCProj1-SetterInjection

        <dependency> 
            <groupId>org.springframework</groupId> 
            <artifactId>spring-context</artifactId> 
            <version>5.3.30</version> 
        </dependency> 
    </dependencies> 
Application Context.Xml: 
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?> 
<beans xmlns="http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans" 
       xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" 
       xsi:schemaLocation=" 
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans  
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans/spring-beans.xsd"> 
    <bean id="dt" class="java.util.Date" /> 
    <bean id="mgc" class="com.SpringIOCMSG.MessageGenerator"> 
        <property name="date" ref="dt" /> 
    </bean> 
</beans> 
Concept    - Explanation 
Bean     - Object managed by Spring container 
ID     - Name used to get the bean from context 
Class     - Fully qualified class name for Spring to instantiate 
Setter Injection   - Spring sets a property using a setter method 
Dependency Injection  - MessageGenerator depends on Date, and Spring 
provides it 
Setter Injection 
package com.SpringIOCMSG; 
import java.util.Date; 
public class MessageGenerator { 
 // Depence Class... 
 private Date date; 
 static { 
  System.out.println("WishMeassageGenerator.Class File is Loading"); 
 } 
 public MessageGenerator() { 
  System.out.println("WishGenerator Object is Instantiated....!"); 
 } 
 public void setDate(Date date) { 
  System.out.println("Wish MessageGenerator.setDate()....."); 
  this.date = date; 
 } 
 public String getMessage(String name) { 
  @SuppressWarnings("deprecation") 
  int hour = date.getHours(); 
  String message = ""; 
  if (hour <= 12) { 
   message = "Hello :: " + name + " Good Morning "; 
  } else if (hour <= 16) { 
   message = "Hello :: " + name + " Good Afternoon "; 
  } else if (hour <= 20) { 
   message = "Hello :: " + name + " Good Evening "; 
  } else { 
   message = "Hello :: " + name + " Good Night "; 
  } 
  return message; 
 } 
} 
Launch App Class: 
package com.SpringIOCMSG; 
// Importing Spring container classes 
import org.springframework.context.ApplicationContext; 
import org.springframework.context.support.ClassPathXmlApplicationContext; 
public class LaunchApp { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        // ✅ 1. Create Spring container by loading XML configuration file 
        // This will read applicationContext.xml from src/main/resources/ 
        // and create all beans defined in it 
        ApplicationContext context = new 
ClassPathXmlApplicationContext("applicationContext.xml"); 
        // ✅ 2. Fetch the MessageGenerator bean from the container using its id 'mgc' 
        // It also performs auto type casting to MessageGenerator class 
        MessageGenerator messageContext = context.getBean("mgc", MessageGenerator.class); 
        // ✅ 3. Call the getMessage() method of MessageGenerator 
        // Passing "SuryaPuthra" as the name to generate a wish message 
        String Result = messageContext.getMessage("SuryaPuthra"); 
        // ✅ 4. Print the result to the console 
        System.out.println("Result :: " + Result); 
    } 
} 
Business Logic Class 
Out Put: 
WishMeassageGenerator.Class File is Loading 
WishGenerator Object is Instantiated....! 
Wish MessageGenerator.setDate()..... 
Result :: Hello :: SuryaPuthra Good Morning  
Constructor Injection in Spring: 
Definition: Constructor Injection is a Spring Dependency Injection (DI) technique where the IOC container uses a 
parameterized constructor to create and initialize the target bean with its dependencies. 
Order of Execution: 
 First, the dependent object is created. 
 Then, the target object is created using a constructor that accepts the dependent object as an argument. 
 Setter Injection vs Constructor Injection: 
 Setter: Target object → then dependency is injected. 
 Constructor: Dependency object → then target object is created. 
XML Syntax: 
<bean id="..." class="..."> 
    <constructor-arg name="..." ref="..." /> 
</bean> 
If you use multiple <constructor-arg> tags, Spring uses the matching multi-parameter constructor to instantiate the bean. 
Attributes: 
<ref>: Used to inject object references (other beans). 
<value>: Used to inject primitive or simple values (e.g., int, String, float). 
applicationContext.xml: 
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?> 
<beans xmlns="http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans" 
       xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" 
       xsi:schemaLocation=" 
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans  
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans/spring-beans.xsd"> 
    <!-- Dependent Bean --> 
    <bean id="dt" class="java.util.Date" /> 
    <!-- Target Bean using Constructor Injection --> 
    <bean id="mgc" class="FirstSpringProject.SpringPrj.MessageGenerator"> 
        <constructor-arg ref="dt"/> 
    </bean> 
</beans> 
Main Class: 
package FirstSpringProject.SpringPrj; 
import org.springframework.context.ApplicationContext; 
import org.springframework.context.support.ClassPathXmlApplicationContext; 
public class App { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        ApplicationContext context = new 
ClassPathXmlApplicationContext("applicationContext.xml"); 
        MessageGenerator generator = context.getBean("mgc", 
MessageGenerator.class); 
        String result = generator.getMessage("Teja"); 
        System.out.println(result); 
    } 
} 
package FirstSpringProject.SpringPrj; 
import java.util.Date; 
public class MessageGenerator { 
 // Dependence Class... 
 private Date date; 
 static { 
  System.out.println("WishMeassageGenerator.Class File is Loading"); 
 } 
 public MessageGenerator() { 
  System.out.println("WishGenerator Object is Instantiated....!"); 
 } 
 public MessageGenerator(Date date) { 
  System.out.println("MessageGenerator Object Created via Constructor Injection"); 
  this.date = date; 
 } 
 public String getMessage(String name) { 
  @SuppressWarnings("deprecation") 
  int hour = date.getHours(); 
  String message = ""; 
  if (hour <= 12) { 
   message = "Hello :: " + name + " Good Morning "; 
  } else if (hour <= 16) { 
   message = "Hello :: " + name + " Good Afternoon "; 
  } else if (hour <= 20) { 
   message = "Hello :: " + name + " Good Evening "; 
  } else { 
   message = "Hello :: " + name + " Good Night "; 
  } 
  return message; 
 } 
} 
Out Put: 
WishMeassageGenerator.Class File is Loading 
MessageGenerator Object Created via 
Constructor Injection 
Hello :: Teja Good Night  
if we place<constructor-arg> tag for 'n' time under bean tag, then IOC container uses "n-PARAM" constructor to create the 
Spring bean class Object. 
Note:  
 <ref> attribute to cfg bean id is based on Spring bean class object injection to target bean class properties. 
 <value> to cfg is to inject "simple values" to Spring bean class properties. 
Interview Question:- 
What happens if we enable both setter injection and construcor injection to bean property? and Tell me which id will be 
injected as final values? 
Ans : Since setter method is called after the constructor execution, we say setter injection overrides the value injected by the 
constructor injection.Values/Object injected by the Setter injection will become final values. 
Memory Map How we say setter injection overrides the value injected by the constructor injection. 
Note: 
Bean id should be unique w.r.t IOC container We can configure 2 spring beans having same class names but we should take 
different bean id. Usage of index/type/name attribute in the <constructor-arg> 
package FirstSpringProject.SpringPrj; 
public class MyDate { 
 private int date; 
 private int month; 
 private int year; 
 public MyDate() { 
  System.out.println("MyDate Bean is 
intiataed...!"); 
 } 
 public void setDate(int date) { 
  this.date = date; 
 } 
 public void setMonth(int month) { 
  this.month = month; 
 } 
 public void setYear(int year) { 
  this.year = year; 
 } 
 public String getFormateDate() 
 { 
  return 
String.format("%02d/%02d/%04d", date,month,year); 
 } 
} 
package FirstSpringProject.SpringPrj; 
import java.time.LocalDateTime; 
public class MessageGenerator { 
 // Dependence Class... 
 private MyDate date; 
 static { 
 System.out.println("WishMeassageGenerator.Cla
ss File is Loading"); 
 } 
 public MessageGenerator() { 
  System.out.println("WishGenerator 
Object is Instantiated....!"); 
 } 
 public MessageGenerator(MyDate date) { 
  System.out.println("MessageGenerator 
Object Created via Constructor Injection"); 
  this.date = date; 
 } 
 public String getMessage(String name) { 
  @SuppressWarnings("deprecation") 
  int hour = 
LocalDateTime.now().getHour(); 
  String message = ""; 
  if (hour >=6 && hour<=12) { 
   message = "Hello :: " + name + " 
Good Morning "; 
  } else if (hour >=12 &&hour <= 16) { 
   message = "Hello :: " + name + " 
Good Afternoon "; 
  } else if (hour >=16 && hour <= 20) { 
   message = "Hello :: " + name + " 
Good Evening "; 
  } else { 
   message = "Hello :: " + name + " 
Good Night "; 
  } 
  return message+" 
"+date.getFormateDate(); 
 } 
}

        String result = generator.getMessage("Teja"); 
        System.out.println(result); 
    } 
}

Usage of index/type/name attribute in the <constructor-arg>: 
If there are mulitple params in constructor and if they have same datatype,then to resolve 
the parameter binding from the container we need to go either index/name(recomended) 
private Integer eno; 
private String ename; 
private float esalary; 
private String eaddress; 
public Employee(Integer eno, String ename, float esalary, String eaddress) { 
 this.eno = eno; 
 this.ename = ename; 
 this.esalary = esalary; 
 this.eaddress = eaddress; 
} 
applicationContext.xml -Injection from container  
<constructor-arg value="MI" type='java.lang.String'/> 
<constructor-arg value="sachin" type='java.lang.String'/> 
<constructor-arg value="3500.05F" type='float'/> 
<constructor-arg value="10" type='java.lang.Integer'/> 
Out Put : Employee [eno=10, ename=MI, esalary=3500.05, eaddress=sachin] 
esolving the mismatch through index 
private String ename; 
private float esalary; 
private String eaddress; 
public Employee(Integer eno, String ename, float esalary, String eaddress) { 
 this.eno = eno; 
 this.ename = ename; 
 this.esalary = esalary; 
 this.eaddress = eaddress; 
} 
applicationContext.xml - Injection from container 
<constructor-arg value="MI" index='3'/> 
<constructor-arg value="sachin" index='1'/> 
<constructor-arg value="3500.05F" index='2'/> 
<constructor-arg value="10" index='0'/> 
Out Put :Employee [eno=10, ename=sachin, esalary=3500.05, eaddress=MI] 
Employee Main Class: 
package FirstSpringProject.SpringPrj; 
import org.springframework.context.ApplicationContext; 
import org.springframework.context.support.ClassPathXmlApplicationContext; 
public class EmployeeMain { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  ApplicationContext context = new 
ClassPathXmlApplicationContext("applicationContext.xml"); 
  Employee emp = context.getBean("emp", Employee.class); 
  String empinfo = emp.toString(); 
  System.out.println("Emp Info : "+emp); 
 } 
} 
Pojo Class:- 
package FirstSpringProject.SpringPrj; 
public class Employee { 
 private String name; 
 private int id; 
 private String address; 
 public Employee(String name, int id, String address) { 
  super(); 
  this.name = name; 
  this.id = id; 
  this.address = address; 
 } 
 public void setName(String name) { 
  this.name = name; 
 } 
 public void setId(int id) { 
  this.id = id; 
 } 
 public void setAddress(String address) { 
  this.address = address; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String toString() { 
  return "Employee [name=" + name + ", id=" + id + ", address=" + address + 
"]"; 
 } 
}

package FirstSpringProject.SpringPrj; 
public class CricketPlayer { 
 private String playerName; 
 private int playerid; 
 private String playerTeam; 
 private String Country; 
 public void setPlayerName(String playerName) { 
  this.playerName = playerName; 
 } 
 public void setPlayerid(int playerid) { 
  this.playerid = playerid; 
 } 
 public void setPlayerTeam(String playerTeam) { 
  this.playerTeam = playerTeam; 
 } 
 public void setCountry(String country) { 
  Country = country; 
 } 
 public CricketPlayer() { 
        System.out.println("CricketPlayer Object created using Default Constructor"); 
    } 
 public CricketPlayer(String playerName, int playerid, String playerTeam, String country) { 
  this.playerName = playerName; 
  this.playerid = playerid; 
  this.playerTeam = playerTeam; 
  Country = country; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String toString() { 
  return "CricketPlayer [playerName=" + playerName + ", playerid=" + playerid + ", 
playerTeam=" + playerTeam 
    + ", Country=" + Country + "]"; 
 } 
} 
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?> 
<beans xmlns="http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans" 
       xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" 
       xsi:schemaLocation=" 
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans  
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans/spring-beans.xsd"> 
  <!-- Cricket Player Bean By Constructor Injection --> 
   <bean id="ply1" class="FirstSpringProject.SpringPrj.CricketPlayer"> 
     <constructor-arg name ="playerName" value = "Virat Kohli" /> 
     <constructor-arg name ="playerid" value = "18" /> 
     <constructor-arg name ="playerTeam" value="RCB"/> 
     <constructor-arg name ="country" value="IND"/> 
  </bean> 
   <!-- Cricket Player Bean By Setter Injection --> 
 <bean id="ply2" class="FirstSpringProject.SpringPrj.CricketPlayer"> 
  <property name="playerName" value="Dhoni" /> 
  <property name="playerid" value="07" /> 
  <property name="playerTeam" value="CSK" /> 
  <property name="country" value="IND" /> 
 </bean> 
</beans> 
package FirstSpringProject.SpringPrj; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.support.DefaultListableBeanFactory; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.xml.XmlBeanDefinitionReader; 
public class CricketPlayersMainClass { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
   DefaultListableBeanFactory factory = new DefaultListableBeanFactory(); 
    XmlBeanDefinitionReader beanreader = new XmlBeanDefinitionReader(factory); 
    beanreader.loadBeanDefinitions("applicationContext.xml"); 
    CricketPlayer player1 = factory.getBean("ply1", CricketPlayer.class); 
    System.out.println("Player Info :: "+player1); 
    System.out.println(); 
    CricketPlayer player2 = factory.getBean("ply2", CricketPlayer.class); 
    System.out.println("Player Info :: "+player2);    
 } 
} 
Out put: 
Player Info :: CricketPlayer 
[playerName=Virat Kohli, playerid=18, 
playerTeam=RCB, Country=IND] 
CricketPlayer Object created using Default 
Constructor 
Player Info :: CricketPlayer 
[playerName=Dhoni, playerid=7, 
playerTeam=CSK, Country=IND] 
D    
Container work flow:- 
 BeanFactory container ========> XmlBeanFactory(Depercated from Spring3.1V) 
 BeanFactory container ========> DefaultListableBeanFactory 
Limitations of XmlBeanFactory: 
 Need of Resource object to hold the name and location of Spring bean configuration file. 
 XmlBeanFactory uses XmlParser to read the bean defnition and to process the xml file 
which is not good in terms of performance. 
 Doesn't allow to take multiple xml files at a time as spring bean configuration file. 
Circular Dependency Injection/Cyclic Dependency Injection 
 It is all about making 2 classes dependent on each other. 
 It is not at all industry practise. 
 Setter injection supports Cyclic Dependency/but Constructor injection doesn't Support Cyclic Dependency. 
 One side Setter and another side Constructor injection would also support " Cyclic Dependency ". 
package com.SpringIOCMSG; 
public class A { 
 private B b; 
 public A() { 
  System.out.println("This 
is Class A Constructor.."); 
 }

package com.SpringIOCMSG; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.support.DefaultListableBeanFactory; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.xml.XmlBeanDefinitionReader; 
public class AbMain { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  DefaultListableBeanFactory factory = new DefaultListableBeanFactory(); 
  XmlBeanDefinitionReader beanreader = new XmlBeanDefinitionReader(factory); 
  beanreader.loadBeanDefinitions("applicationContext.xml"); 
  A a = factory.getBean("a1", A.class); 
  System.out.println(a.getB()); 
  B b = factory.getBean("b1", B.class); 
  System.out.println(b.getA()); 
 } 
} 
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?> 
<beans xmlns="http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans" 
       xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" 
       xsi:schemaLocation=" 
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans  
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans/spring-beans.xsd"> 
    <bean id="a1" class="com.SpringIOCMSG.A"> 
        <property name="b" ref="b1" /> 
    </bean> 
    <bean id="b1" class="com.SpringIOCMSG.B"> 
        <property name="a" ref="a1" /> 
    </bean> 
</beans> 
This is Class A Constructor.. 
This is Class B Constructor 
com.SpringIOCMSG.B@130f889 
com.SpringIOCMSG.A@1188e820 
Difference between Setter injection and Constructor injection:- 
Setter Injection 
 use setter method to inject the dependant values/objects to target class object. 
 <property name='' value=''/> and <property name='' ref=''/> 
 supports cylic dependancy injection 
 bit slow becoz injection happens after creating the Target class object. 
 First Target object and later Dependant object will be created. 
 It is best suited when we want to involve our choice no of properties in Dependency 
injection. 
 If we configure spring bean in setter injection style,then container will create 
 the bean using "zero-arg" constructor. 
Constructor Injection:- 
 use constructor to inject the dependant values/objects to target class object. 
 <constructor-arg name='' value=''/> and <constructor-arg name='' ref=''/> 
 Doesn't supports cylic dependancy injection 
 It is Fast becoz injection happens while instantiating the dependant class object. 
 First Dependant object and later Target object will be created. 
 It is not best suited when we want to involve our choice no of properties in Dependency 
injection,for this we need  overloaded constructor. 
 If we configure spring bean in constructor injection style,then container will 
 create the bean using "n-param" constructor. 
One Project using Spring Core [DI strategy by configuring the container]: 
 VO -> Value Object(it holds the data entered by the user, data would always be in String format only)  
 BO -> Business Object(it holds the actual data which needs to persisted for future usage) 
 DTO-> Data transfer Object(it holds the data in the required data type for processing) 
 Client => String => VO(all variable datatype is String) 
 Controller => String to specific datatype ===> DTO 
 Service => Buisness Object(BO/Model/Entity) gets Generated which will be used in DAO layer.

package com.SpringController; 
import com.CustomerVo.CustomerVo; 
import com.SpringDTO.CustomerDto; 
import com.SpringService.CustomerMgmtService; 
public class CustomerController { 
 CustomerMgmtService service; 
 static 
 { 
  System.out.println("CustomerController  class is Loading....."); 
 } 
 public CustomerController(CustomerMgmtService service) 
 { 
  System.out.println("Main Controller:: one param Constructor...!"); 
  this.service = service; 
 } 
 public String processResult(CustomerVo vo) 
 { 
  String Result =""; 
  try { 
   CustomerDto dto = new CustomerDto(); 
   dto.setCustomerName(vo.getCustomerName()); 
   dto.setCustomeraddress(vo.getCustomeraddress()); 
   dto.setPrincipleAmount(Float.parseFloat(vo.getPrincipleAmount())); 
   dto.setRate(Float.parseFloat(vo.getRate())); 
   dto.setTime(Float.parseFloat(vo.getTime())); 
   String result = service.CalculateSimpleInterest(dto); 
   Result = result; 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  return Result; 
 } 
}

package com.SpringService; 
import com.SpringDTO.CustomerDto; 
public interface CustomerMgmtService { 
    public String CalculateSimpleInterest(CustomerDto dto); 
} 
CustomerMgmtServiceImpl.Java Class: 
package com.SpringService; 
import com.SpringBO.CustomerBo; 
import com.SpringDAO.CustomerDao; 
import com.SpringDTO.CustomerDto; 
public class CustomerMgmtServiceImpl implements CustomerMgmtService { 
 private CustomerDao dao; 
 static 
 { 
  System.out.println("CustomerMgmtServiceImpl class is Loading....."); 
 } 
 public CustomerMgmtServiceImpl(CustomerDao dao) 
 { 
  System.out.println("CustomerMgmtServiceImpl:: Zero Param Constructor....!"); 
  this.dao = dao; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String CalculateSimpleInterest(CustomerDto dto) { 
  Float interestAmount = 0.0f; 
  String message =""; 
  try { 
   interestAmount= 
(dto.getPrincipleAmount()*dto.getTime()*dto.getRate())/100f; 
   CustomerBo bo  = new CustomerBo(); 
   bo.setCustomerName(dto.getCustomerName()); 
   bo.setCustomeraddress(dto.getCustomeraddress()); 
   bo.setPrincipleAmount(dto.getPrincipleAmount()); 
   bo.setRate(dto.getRate()); 
   bo.setTime(dto.getTime()); 
   int count =dao.Insert(bo); 
   if(count==0) 
   { 
    message = "Customer Regstration is Failed :: 
"+dto.getPrincipleAmount()+" Interest Amount Rate :: "+interestAmount; 
   }else 
   { 
    message = "Customer Regstration is Sucessfully :: 
"+dto.getPrincipleAmount()+" Interest Amount Rate :: "+interestAmount; 
   } 
   System.out.println("Message :: "+message); 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  return message; 
 } 
} 
CustomerDao Class: 
package com.SpringDAO; 
import com.SpringBO.CustomerBo; 
public interface CustomerDao { 
 public  int Insert(CustomerBo bo); 
} 
Customer DAO Impl.Java Class: 
package com.SpringDAO; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.PreparedStatement; 
import javax.sql.DataSource; 
import com.SpringBO.CustomerBo; 
public class CustomerDAOImpl implements CustomerDao {  
 private static final String Insert_Query = "Insert Into 
Spring_Customers(Customer_Name,Customer_Address,Principle_Amount,InterestRate,
Time) Values (?,?,?,?,?)"; 
 private DataSource datasource; 
 static 
 { 
  System.out.println("CustomerDAOImpl class is Loading....."); 
 } 
 public CustomerDAOImpl(DataSource datasource) { 
  System.out.println("CustomerDAOImpl :: 1 param Constructor..."); 
  this.datasource = datasource; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public int Insert(CustomerBo bo) { 
  int count = 0; 
  try { 
   Connection connection = datasource.getConnection(); 
   System.out.println("Connection Estiblished Sucessfully...."); 
   PreparedStatement prepareStatement = 
connection.prepareStatement(Insert_Query); 
   prepareStatement.setString(1, bo.getCustomerName()); 
   prepareStatement.setString(2, bo.getCustomeraddress()); 
   prepareStatement.setFloat(3, bo.getPrincipleAmount()); 
   prepareStatement.setFloat(4, bo.getRate()); 
   prepareStatement.setFloat(5, bo.getTime()); 
   count = prepareStatement.executeUpdate(); 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  return count; 
 } 
} 
package com.TestMain; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.support.DefaultListableBeanFactory; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.xml.XmlBeanDefinitionReader; 
import com.CustomerVo.CustomerVo; 
import com.SpringController.CustomerController; 
public class CustomerMain { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in); 
  System.out.print("Enter the Customer Name :: "); 
  String customerName = sc.nextLine(); 
  System.out.print("Enter the Customer Address :: "); 
  String customerAddress = sc.nextLine(); 
  System.out.print("Enter the Customer Amount :: "); 
  String customerAmount = sc.nextLine(); 
  System.out.print("Enter the Customer Time Period :: "); 
  String time = sc.nextLine(); 
  System.out.print("Enter the Rate of Interest :: "); 
  String rate = sc.nextLine(); 
  CustomerVo vo = new CustomerVo(); 
  vo.setCustomeraddress(customerAddress); 
  vo.setCustomerName(customerName); 
  vo.setPrincipleAmount(customerAmount); 
  vo.setTime(time); 
  vo.setRate(rate); 
  DefaultListableBeanFactory factory = new DefaultListableBeanFactory(); 
  XmlBeanDefinitionReader beanreader = new XmlBeanDefinitionReader(factory); 
  beanreader.loadBeanDefinitions("com/SpringConfig/applicationContext.xml"); 
  CustomerController controller = factory.getBean("controller", 
CustomerController.class); 
  String result =controller.processResult(vo); 
  System.out.println(result); 
 } 
}

DB: 
Collection Injection:- 
It is all about injecting values to array,collection type bean properties through Dependancy 
injection. Property type tag/attribute 
simple/primitive <-------> <value> 
object <-------> <ref> 
array <-------> <array>/<list> 
List <-------> <list> 
Set <-------> <set> 
Map <-------> <map> 
Properties <-------> <props>

package com.Spring.IOCCollections; 
import java.util.Arrays; 
import java.util.Date; 
public class MarksInfo { 
 private int marks[]; 
 private Date dates[]; 
 static 
 { 
  System.out.println("MarksInfo Class is Loading"); 
 } 
 public MarksInfo() 
 { 
  System.out.println("MarksInfo zero Param :: Constructor.... "); 
 } 
 public void setMarks(int[] marks) { 
  this.marks = marks; 
 } 
 public void setDates(Date[] dates) { 
  this.dates = dates; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String toString() { 
  return "MarksInfo [marks=" + Arrays.toString(marks) + ", date=" + 
Arrays.toString(dates) + "]"; 
 } 
}

    <entry key="45" value="Rohit" /> 
   </map> 
  </constructor-arg> 
  <property name="dateinfo"> 
   <map key-type="java.lang.String" value-type="java.util.Date"> 
    <entry key="Virat Kohli"> 
     <ref bean="systemDate" /> 
    </entry> 
    <entry key="Sachine"> 
     <ref bean="dojDate" /> 
    </entry> 
    <entry key="Dohni"> 
     <ref bean="SomeDate" /> 
    </entry> 
    <entry key="Rohit"> 
     <ref bean="systemDate" /> 
    </entry> 
   </map> 
  </property> 
  <property name="technology"> 
   <props> 
    <prop key="Core Java">Beginner</prop> 
    <prop key="JDBC">SemiIntermidate</prop> 
    <prop key="Hibernate">Intermidate</prop> 
    <prop key="Spring">Advance</prop> 
    <prop key="Spring-Boot">Expert</prop> 
   </props> 
  </property> 
 </bean> 
</beans>

Null Injection: 
 In constructor injection, all params must participate in injection process otherwise it would result in 
"Exception". 
 If constructor param type is object/reference type and we are not ready with value then we can go for null 
injection. 
 This is very handy(useful) when we are working with predeifned classes as a spring bean, that is a spring bean 
will have limited no of Overloaded constructors and no setter injection support is available. 
syntax: <constructor-arg name=''><null/></constructor-arg> 
applicationcontext.xml: 
<bean id="per2" class='in.ineuron.bean.PersonInfo'> 
 <constructor-arg value='45' /> 
 <constructor-arg value='rohit' /> 
 <constructor-arg name='dob'><null/></constructor-arg> 
 <constructor-arg name='doj'><null /></constructor-arg> 
 <constructor-arg ref="dom" /> 
</bean> 
PersonInfo personInfo2= factory.getBean("per2", PersonInfo.class); 
System.out.println(personInfo2); 
output 
PersonInfo [pno=45, pname=rohit, dob=null, doj=null, dom=Wed Apr 05 12:02:21 IST 2017] 
Bean Inheritance in Spring Core 
Bean inheritance in Spring allows one bean definition to inherit properties from another. This helps reduce duplication and 
improves modularity in XML configuration. 
�
� Why Use Bean Inheritance? 
 Reuse common property configurations. 
 Avoid repeating <property> tags across beans. 
 Easier maintenance of large XML configs. 
Concept     Meaning 
parent     Attribute to indicate which bean to inherit from. 
abstract="true"                Marks a bean as abstract (cannot be instantiated directly). 
Child beans    Can override or extend properties of the parent bean. 
Example:- 
<bean id='baseCar' class="in.ineuron.bean.Car" abstract="true"> 
 <constructor-arg name="engineCC" value='1500' /> 
 <constructor-arg name="model" value='swift' /> 
 <constructor-arg name="company" value='suziki' /> 
 <constructor-arg name="fuelType" value='diesel' /> 
 <constructor-arg name="type" value='hatchback' /> 
</bean> 
<bean id='car1' class='in.ineuron.bean.Car' parent="baseCar"> 
 <constructor-arg name="owner" value='sachin' /> 
 <constructor-arg name="regNo" value='KA4567' /> 
 <constructor-arg name="color" value='red' /> 
 <constructor-arg name="engineNo" value='12345' /> 
</bean> 
<bean id='car2' class='in.ineuron.bean.Car' parent="baseCar"> 
 <constructor-arg name="owner" value='dhoni' /> 
 <constructor-arg name="regNo" value='JH5647' /> 
 <constructor-arg name="color" value='white' /> 
 <constructor-arg name="engineNo" value='56789' /> 
</bean> 
Pojo Class:- 
package com.SpringBeanIneritance; 
public class Car { 
 private String regNo; 
 private String engineNo; 
 private String type; 
 private String model; 
 private String company; 
 private String color; 
 private int engineCC; 
 private String FuelType; 
 private String owner; 
 static 
 { 
  System.out.println("Car.class is loading...."); 
 } 
 public Car() 
 { 
  System.out.println("Car zero param Constructor....!"); 
 } 
 public void setRegNo(String regNo) { 
  this.regNo = regNo; 
 } 
 public void setEngineNo(String engineNo) { 
  this.engineNo = engineNo; 
 } 
 public void setType(String type) { 
  this.type = type; 
 } 
 public void setModel(String model) { 
  this.model = model; 
 } 
 public void setCompany(String company) { 
  this.company = company; 
 } 
 public void setColor(String color) { 
  this.color = color; 
 } 
 public void setEngineCC(int engineCC) { 
  this.engineCC = engineCC; 
 } 
 public void setFuelType(String fuelType) { 
  FuelType = fuelType; 
 } 
 public void setOwner(String owner) { 
  this.owner = owner; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String toString() { 
  return "Car [regNo=" + regNo + ", engineNo=" + engineNo + ", type=" + type 
+ ", model=" + model + ", company=" 
    + company + ", color=" + color + ", engineCC=" + engineCC + ", 
FuelType=" + FuelType + ", owner=" 
    + owner + "]"; 
 } 
}

package com.SpringBeanIneritance; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.support.DefaultListableBeanFactory; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.xml.XmlBeanDefinitionReader; 
public class CarAppMain { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  DefaultListableBeanFactory factory = new DefaultListableBeanFactory(); 
  XmlBeanDefinitionReader reader = new XmlBeanDefinitionReader(factory); 
  reader.loadBeanDefinitions("com/Spring/IOCCollectionsConfig/CarAppContext.xml"); 
  Car car1 = factory.getBean("car1", Car.class); 
  System.out.println(car1); 
  System.out.println(); 
  Car car2 = factory.getBean("car2", Car.class); 
  System.out.println(car2); 
  System.out.println(); 
  Car car3 = factory.getBean("car3", Car.class); 
  System.out.println(car3); 
 } 
}

Important points of inheritance in bean configuration file:- 
1. This is not a class level inheritance, it is spring bean cfg file level bean properties inheritance across multiple spring bean 
cfgs. 
2. <bean abstract='true'> will neve make the class as abstract, but it makes spring bean cfg as abstract. 
3. One spring bean can inherit and reuse the spring bean properties only from one spring bean. Bean inheritance in real-time. 
Bean inheritance in realtime: 
DataSource(I)===> javax.sql.* 
  | 
DriverManagerDataSource(C)===> org.spring.** 
  |

Default Beanid: 
If we don't provide any beadid to the bean, then IOC container will give the default bean id with the following syntax. 
Syntax: <pkg>.<className>#<n> ===> 0 based index

import org.springframework.beans.factory.support.DefaultListableBeanFactory;

public class CarAppMain { 
 public static void main(String[] args) {

  XmlBeanDefinitionReader reader = new XmlBeanDefinitionReader(factory); 
  reader.loadBeanDefinitions("com/Spring/IOCCollectionsConfig/CarAppContext.xml"); 
  Car car1 = factory.getBean("com.SpringBeanIneritance.Car#0", Car.class); 
  System.out.println(car1); 
  System.out.println();

  System.out.println(car2); 
  System.out.println(); 
  Car car3 = factory.getBean("com.SpringBeanIneritance.Car#2", Car.class); 
  System.out.println(car3); 
 } 
}

Auto wiring: 
Assigning the dependant class object to target class object is called "Dependancy 
injection"/"AutoWiring". 
Autowiring can be done in 2 ways 
 a. Explicit Autowiring/Manual Injection 
  a. <property name='' ref=''/> 
  b. <constructor-arg name='' ref=''/> 
 b. Autowiring/AutoInjection 
 <bean id ='' class='' autowire=''/> 
  autowire will take 3 values 
  a. byName 
  b. byType 
  c. constructor 
Note: Autowiring is very useful becoz it helps in RAD(Rapid Application Development). 
Limitations of Autowiring: 
1. It is possible only on Object-type/reference-type bean properties. 
2. There is a possibility of getting Ambiguity problem. 
3. It will also kill readability of Spring bean configuration file. 
Autowire - byName:- 
* Performs Setter Injection 
* Container detects/finds dependent spring bean class object based on id that is matching with 
target class property name(Courier courier; <bean id ='courier' class='in.ineuron.bean.BlueDart'/>) 
* There is no possibility of ambiguity problem becoz the bean id in IOC container 
are unique id's. 
IOC Container – AutoWireing By-Name:- 
Courier Interface:- 
package com.SpringBeanAutowireing; 
public interface Courier { 
 public String deliver(int oid); 
} 
package com.SpringBeanAutowireing; 
public class BlueDart implements Courier { 
 static 
 { 
  System.out.println("BlueDart class is Loading....."); } 
 public BlueDart() 
 { 
  System.out.println("BlueDart object is instantiated..."); 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String deliver(int oid) { 
  System.out.println("BlueDart is Delivered.....!"); 
  return "BlueDart Courier will deliver with Order Id :: "+oid+" Order 
Product"; 
 } 
} 
package com.SpringBeanAutowireing; 
public class DTDC implements Courier { 
 static { 
  System.out.println("DTDC.class file is loading..."); 
 } 
 public DTDC() { 
  System.out.println("DTDC object is created..."); 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String deliver(int oid) { 
  return "DTDC Courier will deliver with Order ID :: "+oid+" 
Order Products"; 
 } 
} 
package com.SpringBeanAutowireing; 
public class FirstFlight implements Courier { 
 static { 
  System.out.println("FirstFlight.class file is loading..."); 
 } 
 public FirstFlight() { 
  System.out.println("FirstFlight object is created..."); 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String deliver(int oid) { 
  return "FirstFlight courier will deliver with the order id :: " + oid + " 
order products"; 
 } 
} 
package com.SpringBeanAutowireing; 
import java.util.Arrays; 
import java.util.Random; 
public class Flipkart { 
 private Courier courier; 
 private Long regNo; 
 static { 
  System.out.println("Flipkart.class file is loading...");} 
 public Flipkart() 
 { 
  System.out.println("Flipkart object is created..."); 
 } 
 public Flipkart(Courier courier, Long regNo) { 
  System.out.println("FlipKart :: Two Param Constructor...!"); 
  this.courier = courier; 
  this.regNo = regNo; 
 } 
 public Flipkart(Courier courier) { 
  System.out.println("Flipkart object is created through Constructor:: One param constructor"); 
  this.courier = courier; 
 } 
 public void setCourier(Courier courier) { 
  this.courier = courier; 
  System.out.println("Courier object is injected through Setter"); 
 } 
 public void setRegNo(Long regNo) { 
  this.regNo = regNo; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String toString() { 
  return "Flipkart [courier=" + courier + ", regNo=" + regNo + "]"; 
 } 
 //Business Logic  
 public String shopping(String[] items,Float[] prices) 
 { 
  System.out.println("Flipkart.shopping()"); 
  System.out.println(courier.getClass().getName()); 
  String res = ""; 
  try { 
    Random random =null; 
    float bill = 0.0f; 
    int oid =0; 
    for(float price : prices) 
    { 
     bill+=price; 
    } 
    random = new Random(); 
    oid = random.nextInt(1000); 
    String msg = courier.deliver(oid); 
    res = Arrays.toString(items) + "are Purchased haveing Prices "+Arrays.toString(prices) 
    +" with bill Amount :: "+bill+" <----> "+msg; 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  return res; 
 } 
} 
Spring-Config.Xml – By Name:- 
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?> 
<beans xmlns="http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans" 
       xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" 
       xsi:schemaLocation=" 
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans  
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans/spring-beans.xsd"> 
     <!-- CONFIGURING THE DEPENDANT BEAN --> 
   <bean id = "courier" class ="com.SpringBeanAutowireing.BlueDart"/> 
   <bean id = "dtdc" class ="com.SpringBeanAutowireing.DTDC"/> 
   <bean id = "firstFlight" class ="com.SpringBeanAutowireing.FirstFlight"/> 
   <!-- CONFIGURING THE TARGET BEAN --> 
   <bean id="flipKart" class ="com.SpringBeanAutowireing.Flipkart" autowire="byName"/> 
</beans> 
package com.MainApps; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.support.DefaultListableBeanFactory; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.xml.XmlBeanDefinitionReader; 
import com.SpringBeanAutowireing.Flipkart; 
public class CourierMainByName { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  DefaultListableBeanFactory factory = new DefaultListableBeanFactory(); 
  XmlBeanDefinitionReader reader = new XmlBeanDefinitionReader(factory); 
  reader.loadBeanDefinitions("com/SpringConfig/SpringConfig.xml"); 
  Flipkart flipKart = factory.getBean("flipKart", Flipkart.class); 
  String result = flipKart.shopping(new String[] {"Noise Smart 
Band","Puma","Iphone"}, new Float[]{3123.33f,1500.65f,64999.56f}); 
  System.out.println(result); 
 } 
}

Flipkart object is created... 
BlueDart class is Loading..... 
BlueDart object is instantiated... 
Courier object is injected through Setter 
Flipkart.shopping() 
com.SpringBeanAutowireing.BlueDart 
BlueDart is Delivered.....! 
[Noise Smart Band, Puma, Iphone]are Purchased haveing Prices [3123.33, 1500.65, 64999.56] 
with bill Amount :: 69623.54 <----> BlueDart Courier will deliver with Order Id :: 315 Order 
Product 
Autowire - byType:- 
 Perform Setter Injection 
 Container detects/finds dependant spring bean class object based 
on the property type/class type     in the Target class(Courier 
courier;* It is Courier type) 
 There is a possiblity of Ambiguity problem and we solve this 
problem by using "primary=true" in one of the dependent spring 
bean configuration. 
byType:- 
SpringConfiguredbyAutowiredByType.Xml:- 
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?> 
<beans xmlns="http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans" 
       xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" 
       xsi:schemaLocation=" 
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans  
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans/spring-beans.xsd"> 
     <!-- CONFIGURING THE DEPENDANT BEAN --> 
   <bean id = "courier" class ="com.SpringBeanAutowireing.BlueDart"/> 
   <bean id = "dtdc" class ="com.SpringBeanAutowireing.DTDC" primary ="true"/> 
   <bean id = "firstFlight" class ="com.SpringBeanAutowireing.FirstFlight"/> 
   <!-- CONFIGURING THE TARGET BEAN --> 
   <bean id="flipKart" class ="com.SpringBeanAutowireing.Flipkart" autowire="byType"/> 
</beans> 
package com.MainApps; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.support.DefaultListableBeanFactory; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.xml.XmlBeanDefinitionReader; 
import com.SpringBeanAutowireing.Flipkart; 
public class CourierMainByType { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  DefaultListableBeanFactory factory = new DefaultListableBeanFactory(); 
  XmlBeanDefinitionReader reader = new XmlBeanDefinitionReader(factory); 
 reader.loadBeanDefinitions("com/SpringConfig/SpringConfigAutowiredByType.xml"); 
  Flipkart flipKart = factory.getBean("flipKart", Flipkart.class); 
  String result = flipKart.shopping(new String[] {"Noise Smart 
Band","Puma","Iphone"}, new Float[] 
    {3123.33f,1500.65f,64999.56f}); 
  System.out.println(result); 
 } 
}

autowire - constructor:- 
* Performs constuctor injection using paramatereized constructor 
* Here constructor param name should match with Dependant class bean id for the autowiring to happen. 
* There is no possiblity of ambiguity problem becoz the bean id in IOC container are unique id's. 
Note: if we keep id name and consturctor param name same and in any one of the bean. 
with primary = true, then 
constructor injection will happen by giving the priority for primary=true. 
autowire-candidate - false 
*If we don't want particular beans not to participate in autowiring then we use the above property 
*It is one more solution to resolve the problem of ambiguity which would arise in 
byType. 
 <!-- CONFIGURING THE DEPENDANT BEAN --> 
 <bean id='bDart' class='in.ineuron.bean.BlueDart' /> 
 <bean id='dtdc' class='in.ineuron.bean.DTDC' autowire-candidate="false" 
 primary="true"/> //invalid combo 
 <bean id='courier' class='in.ineuron.bean.FirstFlight' autowire- 
 candidate="false"/> 
 <!-- CONFIGURING THE TARGET BEAN --> 
 <bean id='fpkt' class='in.ineuron.bean.Flipkart' autowire="byType"> 
  <property name="regNo" value='12345' /> 
 </bean> 
SpringConfigConstructor AutoWireing.xml:- 
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?> 
<beans xmlns="http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans" 
       xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" 
       xsi:schemaLocation=" 
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans  
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans/spring-beans.xsd"> 
     <!-- CONFIGURING THE DEPENDANT BEAN --> 
   <bean id = "courier" class ="com.SpringBeanAutowireing.BlueDart"/> 
   <bean id = "dtdc" class ="com.SpringBeanAutowireing.DTDC" primary="true"/> 
   <bean id = "firstFlight" class ="com.SpringBeanAutowireing.FirstFlight"/> 
   <!-- CONFIGURING THE TARGET BEAN --> 
   <bean id="flipKart" class ="com.SpringBeanAutowireing.Flipkart" autowire="constructor"> 
      <property name="regNo" value='12345' /> 
   </bean> 
</beans> 
Constructor Auto-Wireing:- 
package com.MainApps; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.support.DefaultListableBeanFactory; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.xml.XmlBeanDefinitionReader; 
import com.SpringBeanAutowireing.Flipkart; 
public class CourierConstructorMain { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  DefaultListableBeanFactory factory = new DefaultListableBeanFactory(); 
  XmlBeanDefinitionReader reader = new XmlBeanDefinitionReader(factory); 
 reader.loadBeanDefinitions("com/SpringConfig/SpringConfigAutoWiredByConstructor.xml
"); 
  Flipkart flipKart = factory.getBean("flipKart", Flipkart.class); 
  String result = flipKart.shopping(new String[] {"Noise Smart 
Band","Puma","Iphone"}, new Float[] 
    {3123.33f,1500.65f,64999.56f}); 
  System.out.println(result); 
 } 
}

Scope attribute in Spring:- 
 Singleton(default):- 
 It is the default scope for a particular bean in spring. 
 IOC container will never make spring bean class as singleton java class, but it creates only one object, keeps 
that object in internal cache and returns that object every time we make a call tofactory.getBean(). 
ApplicationContext.Xml:- 
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?> 
<beans xmlns="http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans" 
       xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" 
       xsi:schemaLocation=" 
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans  
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans/spring-beans.xsd"> 
    <!-- Dependent Bean --> 
 <bean id="dt" class="com.SpringAttributes.MyDate"> 
  <property name="date" value="20" /> 
  <property name="month" value="06" /> 
  <property name="year" value="2025" /> 
 </bean> 
    <!-- Target Bean using Constructor Injection --> 
    <bean id="mgc" class="com.SpringAttributes.MessageGenerator" scope="singleton"> 
        <constructor-arg name ="date" ref="dt"/> 
    </bean> 
</beans> 
package com.SpringAttributes; 
import org.springframework.context.ApplicationContext; 
import org.springframework.context.support.ClassPathXmlApplicationContext; 
public class App { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        ApplicationContext context = new 
ClassPathXmlApplicationContext("com/SpringAttributeConfig/applicationContext.xml"); 
        MessageGenerator generator1 = context.getBean("mgc", MessageGenerator.class); 
        String result = generator1.getMessage("Teja"); 
        MessageGenerator generator2 = context.getBean("mgc", MessageGenerator.class); 
        String result2 = generator2.getMessage("Teja"); 
        System.out.println("Generator1 Class Referance Object :: "+generator1.hashCode()); 
        System.out.println("Generator2 Class Referance Object :: "+generator2.hashCode()); 
        System.out.println("\n"); 
        System.out.println(result+ " \t\t\t "+result2); 
    } 
}

Prototype:- 
 IOC container creates a new object for Spring bean class for every factory.getBean() method. 
 IOC container doesn't keep this scope spring bean class objects in "internal cache" of IOC 
container. 
AppContext.xml:- 
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?> 
<beans xmlns="http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans" 
       xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" 
       xsi:schemaLocation=" 
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans  
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans/spring
beans.xsd"> 
    <!-- Dependent Bean --> 
 <bean id="dt" class="com.SpringAttributes.MyDate"> 
  <property name="date" value="20" /> 
  <property name="month" value="06" /> 
  <property name="year" value="2025" /> 
 </bean> 
    <!-- Target Bean using Constructor Injection --> 
    <bean id="mgc" class="com.SpringAttributes.MessageGenerator" 
scope="prototype"> 
        <constructor-arg name ="date" ref="dt"/> 
    </bean> 
</beans> 
package com.SpringAttributes; 
import org.springframework.context.ApplicationContext; 
import org.springframework.context.support.ClassPathXmlApplicationContext; 
public class AppScopePrototype { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        ApplicationContext context = new 
ClassPathXmlApplicationContext("com/SpringAttributeConfig/appContextScopePrototype.xml"); 
        MessageGenerator generator1 = context.getBean("mgc", MessageGenerator.class); 
        String result = generator1.getMessage("Teja"); 
        MessageGenerator generator2 = context.getBean("mgc", MessageGenerator.class); 
        String result2 = generator2.getMessage("Teja"); 
        System.out.println("Generator1 Class Referance Object :: "+generator1.hashCode()); 
        System.out.println("Generator2 Class Referance Object :: "+generator2.hashCode()); 
        System.out.println("\n"); 
        System.out.println(result+ " \t\t\t "+result2); 
    } 
}

ApplicationContext container:- 
1. It is an extension of BeanFactory 
2. Implementation classes of ApplicationContext(I). 
 a. FileSystemXmlApplicationContext(standalone). 
 b. ClassPathXmlApplicationContext(standalone). 
 c. XmlWebApplicationContext(SpringMVC apps). 
 d. AnnotationConfigApplicationContext(Standaloneapp's). 
 e. AnnotationConfigWebApplicationContext(SpringMVC apps). 
Additional features of Application Context container:- 
1. PreInstantiation of SingletonScope beans. 
 Container will create an object for all the beans which are configured under "singleton" scope. 
 Container will never wait till context.getBean() is called. 
 This feature is very useful in "SpringMVC" to configure the "DispatcherServlet" which is the Controller. 
If we want to disable the preinstantiation of SingletonScope beans then we need to 
use 
<bean id='bDart' class='in.ineuron.bean.BlueDart' lazy-init="true"/> 
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?> 
<beans xmlns="http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans" 
 xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" 
 xsi:schemaLocation="http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans  
                           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans/spring-beans.xsd"> 
 <!-- CONFIGURING THE DEPENDANT BEAN --> 
 <bean id="courier" class="com.SpringBeanAutowireing.BlueDart" lazy-init="true" /> 
 <bean id="dtdc" class="com.SpringBeanAutowireing.DTDC"/> 
 <bean id="firstFlight" class="com.SpringBeanAutowireing.FirstFlight" autowire-candidate="false" lazy
init="true" /> 
 <!-- CONFIGURING THE TARGET BEAN --> 
 <bean id="flipKart" class="com.SpringBeanAutowireing.Flipkart" 
  autowire="constructor"> 
  <property name="regNo" value='12345' /> 
 </bean> 
</beans> 
Lazy Loading of Bean  
package com.MainApps; 
import org.springframework.context.ApplicationContext; 
import org.springframework.context.support.ClassPathXmlApplicationContext; 
import com.SpringBeanAutowireing.Flipkart; 
public class CourierMainLazyLoading { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  ApplicationContext context = new 
ClassPathXmlApplicationContext("com/SpringConfig/LazyLoadingConfig.xml"); 
  System.out.println("IOC container created..."); 
  Flipkart flipkart = context.getBean("flipKart", Flipkart.class); 
  System.out.println(flipkart.shopping(new String[] { "fossil", "cryzal" }, new Float[] { 
3000.0f, 3000.0f })); 
 } 
}

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?> 
<beans xmlns="http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans" 
       xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" 
       xsi:schemaLocation=" 
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans  
           http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans/spring-beans.xsd"> 
    <!-- Load properties file --> 
    <bean id="properties" 
class="org.springframework.beans.factory.config.PropertyPlaceholderConfigurer"> 
        <property name="location" value="classpath:com/SpringJDBCProperties/application.properties"/> 
    </bean> 
    <!-- Data Source Configuration --> 
    <bean id="mysqlDataSource" class="org.springframework.jdbc.datasource.DriverManagerDataSource"> 
        <property name="driverClassName" value="${jdbc.driver}"/> 
        <property name="username" value="${jdbc.user}"/> 
        <property name="password" value="${jdbc.password}"/>  
    </bean> 
    <!-- HikariCP Configuration --> 
    <bean id="hikariDataSource" class="com.zaxxer.hikari.HikariDataSource" parent ="mysqlDataSource"> 
     <property name="jdbcUrl" value="${jdbc.url}"/> 
        <property name="minimumIdle" value="10"/> 
        <property name="maximumPoolSize" value="20"/> 
        <property name="connectionTimeout" value="2000"/> 
    </bean> 
    <!-- DAO Configuration -->  
    <bean id="mysqlDao" class="com.SpringDAO.CustomerDAOImpl"> 
        <constructor-arg name="datasource" ref="hikariDataSource"/> 
    </bean> 
    <!-- Service Configuration -->  
    <bean id="service" class="com.SpringService.CustomerMgmtServiceImpl"> 
        <constructor-arg name="dao" ref="mysqlDao"/>  
    </bean> 
    <!-- Controller Configuration --> 
    <bean id="controller" class="com.SpringController.CustomerController"> 
        <constructor-arg name="service" ref="service"/>  
    </bean> 
</beans>

package com.TestMain; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.support.DefaultListableBeanFactory; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.xml.XmlBeanDefinitionReader; 
import org.springframework.context.support.ClassPathXmlApplicationContext; 
import com.CustomerVo.CustomerVo; 
import com.SpringController.CustomerController; 
public class CustomerAppPropertyTest { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
 ClassPathXmlApplicationContext factory = new 
ClassPathXmlApplicationContext("com/SpringConfig/applicationContextappProperties.xml"); 
  CustomerController controller = factory.getBean("controller", CustomerController.class); 
  CustomerVo vo = InserCustomerData(); 
  String result1 =controller.processResult(vo); 
  System.out.println(result1); 
  System.out.println("\t"); 
  int cid = getCustomerInfo(); 
  String result = controller.GetCustomerInfoById(cid); 
  System.out.println(result); 
 } 
 public static CustomerVo  InserCustomerData() 
 { 
  Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in); 
  System.out.print("Enter the Customer Name :: "); 
  String customerName = sc.nextLine(); 
  System.out.print("Enter the Customer Address :: "); 
  String customerAddress = sc.nextLine(); 
  System.out.print("Enter the Customer Amount :: "); 
  String customerAmount = sc.nextLine(); 
  System.out.print("Enter the Customer Time Period :: "); 
  String time = sc.nextLine(); 
  System.out.print("Enter the Rate of Interest :: "); 
  String rate = sc.nextLine(); 
  CustomerVo vo = new CustomerVo(); 
  vo.setCustomeraddress(customerAddress); 
  vo.setCustomerName(customerName); 
  vo.setPrincipleAmount(customerAmount); 
  vo.setTime(time); 
  vo.setRate(rate); 
  return vo; 
 } 
 public static int getCustomerInfo() 
 { 
  Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in); 
  System.out.print("Enter the Customer Id :: "); 
  int CID = sc.nextInt(); 
  return CID; 
 } 
}

location="classpath:com/SpringJDBCProperties/application.properties"/>

        <property name="driverClassName" value="${jdbc.driver}"/> 
        <property name="jdbcUrl" value="${jdbc.url}"/>

        <property name="password" value="${jdbc.password}"/>

        <constructor-arg name="dao" ref="mysqlDao"/>  
    </bean>

        <constructor-arg name="service" ref="service"/>  
    </bean> 
</beans>

Support of I18N(Internationalization) 
 Making our application work for all different locale is called I18N. 
 Locale -- Langauge+ Country 
 eg: en-US,en-BR,hi-IN,fr-FR,de-DE,.....

package com.SpringIOCInternallization; 
import java.util.Locale; 
import org.springframework.context.support.ClassPathXmlApplicationContext; 
public class ClientTestApp { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        ClassPathXmlApplicationContext context = 
                new 
ClassPathXmlApplicationContext("com/IOCSpringInternalizationConfig/SpringIocInternalizationContext.xml"); 
     //   Locale locale = (args.length >= 2) ? new Locale(args[0], args[1]) : Locale.getDefault(); 
 Locale locale = new Locale("te","IN"); 
        String cap1 = context.getMessage("btn1.cap", null, "msg1", locale); 
        String cap2 = context.getMessage("btn2.cap", null, "msg2", locale); 
        String cap3 = context.getMessage("btn3.cap", null, "msg3", locale); 
        String cap4 = context.getMessage("btn4.cap", null, "msg4", locale); 
        System.out.println(cap1 + " | " + cap2 + " | " + cap3 + " | " + cap4); 
        System.out.println(); 
        // Hardcoded examples 
        System.out.println(context.getMessage("btn1.cap", null, new Locale("en", "US"))); 
        System.out.println(context.getMessage("btn2.cap", null, new Locale("hi", "IN"))); 
        System.out.println(context.getMessage("btn3.cap", null, new Locale("fr", "FR"))); 
        System.out.println(context.getMessage("btn4.cap", null, new Locale("de", "De"))); 
        System.out.println(context.getMessage("btn3.cap", null, new Locale("te", "IN"))); 
        System.out.println(context.getMessage("btn2.cap", null, new Locale("tm", "IN"))); 
        context.close(); 
    } 
}

Spring Annotations Explanation 
1. @Configuration- Marks a class as a source of bean definitions for the Spring IoC container.- Similar to 
`applicationContext.xml` in XML-based configuration. 
2. @Required- Applied on setter methods to indicate that the property must be populated at configuration 
time.- Deprecated since Spring 5 due to constructor injection preference. 
3. @Repository- Specialization of `@Component`, used to indicate that the class provides the mechanism 
for storage, retrieval, search, update, and delete operations on objects.- Converts JPA/Hibernate exceptions 
into Spring's DataAccessException. 
4. @Order- Specifies the order of execution for components or aspects.- Lower values have higher priority. 
5. @Autowired- Automatically injects dependencies by type.- Can be used on constructors, fields, or setter 
methods. 
6. @Qualifier- Used along with `@Autowired` to resolve ambiguity when multiple beans of the same type 
exist.- Specifies the name of the bean to inject. 
7. @Scope- Defines the scope of a Spring bean (e.g., singleton, prototype, request, session). 
8. @Component- Indicates that the class is a Spring-managed component.- Generic stereotype for any 
Spring-managed component. 
9. @Service- Specialization of `@Component`, indicates a service class in the business layer. 
10. @Controller- Specialization of `@Component`, indicates a web controller.- Used in Spring MVC to 
handle web reque 
11. @Bean- Indicates that a method produces a bean to be managed by the Spring container.- Used inside a 
`@Configuration` class. 
12. @DependsOn- Specifies the names of the beans that should be initialized before the current bean. 
13. @Lazy- Indicates that a bean should not be initialized until it is requested.- Can be used at the class or 
bean definition level. 
14. @Value- Injects values into fields from property files or system properties. 
15. @Import- Allows importing additional `@Configuration` classes.- Useful to modularize configuration. 
16. @ImportResource- Imports XML-based configuration into a Java-based configuration class. 
17. @ComponentScan- Tells Spring where to search for annotated components (`@Component`, 
`@Service`, `@Repository`, `@Controller`). 
18. @PropertySource- Declares a `.properties` file to be loaded by the application context.- Used with 
`@Value`. 
19. @Primary- Marks a bean as the primary candidate for autowiring when multiple beans of the same 
type are present. 
20. @Lookup- Used to inject prototype-scoped beans into singleton beans.- Tells Spring to override the 
method to return a new instance each time. 
21. @PostConstruct- Method annotated with this will be executed after dependency injection is done.- 
Comes from `javax.annotation` package. 
22. @PreDestroy- Method annotated with this will be executed before the bean is removed from the 
context.- Also comes from `javax.annotation` package 
Component Scanning & Dependency  Injection : 
• @Component : Marks a class as a Spring-managed  component. Used for generic components that 
don't fit      into @Service, @Repository, or @Controller categories.   
• @Controller : Specialized @Component, used in Spring MVC to define a web controller.   
• @RestController : Combines @Controller and  
• @ResponseBody to simplify RESTful API development.  
• @Service : Specialized @Component, used for business logic and service layer components.   
• @Repository : Specialized @Component, used for data access objects (DAO) to indicate storage 
operations.   
• @Autowired : Automatically injects dependencies into Spring beans, reducing manual configuration.  
•  @Qualifier("beanName") : Specifies which bean to inject when multiple candidates exist.   
•  @Primary : Marks a bean as the default choice when multiple candidates exist.   
• @Value("${property.key}") : Injects values from properties files into Spring beans. 
Mode of Spring application development:- 
1. XML Driven 
2. Annotation driven configuration 
3. 100% code driven cfgs(pure java/no xml) 
4. Spring boot driven configuration 
Annotation driven Configuration:- 
1. @Required(Deprecated from 5.1V of Spring) 
* While working with parameterized constructor injection we must configure all params of 
that constructor injection.if we fail to do it would result in "Exception". 
* This restriction is not available if we work with "Setter Injection". 
* To bring such restriction on choice of our bean properties through 
Setter injection, we need to go for @Required. 
Note: 
The entire functionality of @Required annotation is placed inside a ready made 
class called "RequiredAnnotationBeanPostProcessor". 
So to use annotations in our application we need to configure the above class as 
"Spring bean". 
Configuring BeanPostProcessor for every annoation seperately is a complex process, 
to overcome this problem just use 
<context:annotation-config/> in spring bean configuration file. 
The above code in the configuration file would activate the following annotations 
@Required,@Autowired,@PostConstruct,@PreDestroy,@Resource,..... 
Note: 
@Required is deprecated in Spring5.1, saying to go for consturctor injection in 
order to add restrictions on injection. 
ApplicationContext.xml : 
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?> 
<beans xmlns="http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans" 
    xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" 
    xmlns:context="http://www.springframework.org/schema/context" 
    xsi:schemaLocation="http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans 
        https://www.springframework.org/schema/beans/spring-beans.xsd 
        http://www.springframework.org/schema/context 
        https://www.springframework.org/schema/context/spring-context.xsd"> 
 <bean id='robot' class='com.SpringRequired.Robot'> 
  <property name="id" value="10000"/> 
  <property name="name" value="VenexSCAR3"/> 
  <property name="lab" value="TSNAKA GSHA" /> 
  <property name="price" value="54335" /> 
 </bean> 
   <context:annotation-config/> 
</beans> 
package com.SpringRequired; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Required; 
public class Robot { 
 private Integer id = 123; 
 private String name; 
 private String lab; 
 private double price; 
 public Integer getId() { 
  return id; 
 } 
 @Required 
 public void setId(Integer id) { 
  this.id = id; 
 } 
 public String getName() { 
  return name; 
 } 
 @Required 
 public void setName(String name) { 
  this.name = name; 
 } 
 public String getLab() { 
  return lab; 
 } 
 public void setLab(String lab) { 
  this.lab = lab; 
 } 
 public double getPrice() { 
  return price; 
 } 
 public void setPrice(double price) { 
  this.price = price; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String toString() { 
  return "Robot [id=" + id + ", name=" + name + ", lab=" + lab + ", price=" + 
price + "]"; 
 } 
} 
To read the Annotations 
We must need to Config 
this in AppContext.xml 
file. 
package com.SpringRequired; 
import org.springframework.context.support.ClassPathXmlApplicationContext; 
public class RobotMain { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  ClassPathXmlApplicationContext context = new 
ClassPathXmlApplicationContext("com/IOCSpringInternalizationConfig/RequiredAppContext.xml"); 
     Robot robot = context.getBean("robot", Robot.class); 
     System.out.println(robot); 
 } 
} 
Robot [id=10000, name=VenexSCAR3, lab=TSNAKA GSHA, 
price=54335.0] 
<bean id='robot' class='com.SpringRequired.Robot'> 
  <property name="id" value="10000"/> 
  <property name="price" value="54335" /> 
 </bean> 
   <context:annotation-config/> 
Robot [id=10000, name=null, lab=null, price=54335.0] 
2.@Autowired 
* Performs byType,byName,Constructor mode of autowiring(detecting the dependent bean  
dynamically without using <property> and <constructor-arg> tags) 
* Can be applied on field level(instance variables),constructor,setter methods. 
* It cannot be used to inject values to simple properties, can be used to injection values only to  Object 
type/ref type. 
*Through annotation support, without setter/constructor still injection can be done through "instance  
variables", where spring uses "Reflection API" to access private properties of a class. 
*Default Autowiring is based on byType. 
AppContext.xml: 
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?> 
<beans xmlns="http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans" 
 xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" 
 xmlns:context="http://www.springframework.org/schema/context" 
 xsi:schemaLocation="http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans 
        https://www.springframework.org/schema/beans/spring-beans.xsd 
        http://www.springframework.org/schema/context 
        https://www.springframework.org/schema/context/spring-context.xsd"> 
 <!-- Config the Annotations in the XMl --> 
 <context:annotation-config /> 
 <!-- CONFIGURING THE DEPENDANT BEAN --> 
<bean id='fFlight' class='com.Spring.ByAnnotationAutowireing.FirstFlight' /> 
 <bean id='dtdc' class='com.Spring.ByAnnotationAutowireing.DTDC'/> 
 <bean id="courier" class='com.Spring.ByAnnotationAutowireing.BlueDart' /> 
 <!-- CONFIGURING THE TARGET BEAN --> 
 <bean id='fpkt' class='com.Spring.ByAnnotationAutowireing.Flipkart' /> 
</beans> 
package com.Spring.ByAnnotationAutowireing; 
public interface Courier { 
 public String deliver(int oid); 
} 
package com.Spring.ByAnnotationAutowireing; 
public class BlueDart implements Courier { 
 static 
 { 
  System.out.println("BlueDart class is Loading....."); 
 } 
 public BlueDart() 
 { 
  System.out.println("BlueDart object is instantiated..."); 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String deliver(int oid) { 
  System.out.println("BlueDart is Delivered.....!"); 
  return "BlueDart Courier will deliver with Order Id :: "+oid+" Order Product"; 
 } 
} 
package com.Spring.ByAnnotationAutowireing; 
public class DTDC implements Courier { 
 static { 
  System.out.println("DTDC.class file is loading..."); 
 } 
 public DTDC() { 
  System.out.println("DTDC object is created..."); 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String deliver(int oid) { 
  return "DTDC Courier will deliver with Order ID :: "+oid+" Order Products"; 
 } 
}

<bean id='fFlight' class='com.Spring.ByAnnotationAutowireing.FirstFlight' /> 
 <bean id='dtdc' class='com.Spring.ByAnnotationAutowireing.DTDC'/> 
 <bean id="bDart" class='com.Spring.ByAnnotationAutowireing.BlueDart' /> 
 <!-- CONFIGURING THE TARGET BEAN --> 
 <bean id='fpkt' class='com.Spring.ByAnnotationAutowireing.Flipkart' /> 
package com.Spring.ByAnnotationAutowireing; 
import java.util.Arrays; 
import java.util.Random; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired; 
public class Flipkart { 
 //Feild level Autowireing ... 
 @Autowired 
 private Courier courier; 
 private Long regNo; 
 static { 
  System.out.println("Flipkart.class file is loading..."); 
 } 
 public Flipkart() 
 { 
  System.out.println("Flipkart object is created..."); 
 } 
 public Flipkart(Courier courier, Long regNo) { 
  System.out.println("FlipKart :: Two Param Constructor...!"); 
  this.courier = courier; 
  this.regNo = regNo; 
 } 
 public Flipkart(Courier courier) { 
  System.out.println("Flipkart object is created through Constructor:: One param 
constructor"); 
  this.courier = courier; 
 } 
 public void setCourier(Courier courier) { 
  this.courier = courier; 
  System.out.println("Courier object is injected through Setter"); 
 } 
 public void setRegNo(Long regNo) { 
  this.regNo = regNo; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String toString() { 
  return "Flipkart [courier=" + courier + ", regNo=" + regNo + "]"; 
 } 
 //Business Logic  
 public String shopping(String[] items,Float[] prices) 
 { 
  System.out.println("Flipkart.shopping()"); 
  System.out.println(courier.getClass().getName()); 
  String res = ""; 
  try { 
    Random random =null; 
    float bill = 0.0f; 
    int oid =0; 
    for(float price : prices) 
    { 
     bill+=price; 
    } 
    random = new Random(); 
    oid = random.nextInt(1000); 
    String msg = courier.deliver(oid); 
    res = Arrays.toString(items) + "are Purchased haveing Prices 
"+Arrays.toString(prices) 
    +" with bill Amount :: "+bill+" <----> "+msg; 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  return res; 
 } 
} 
Field Level 
AutoWireing 
package com.Spring.ByAnnotationAutowireingMainApp; 
import org.springframework.context.support.ClassPathXmlApplicationContext; 
import com.Spring.ByAnnotationAutowireing.Flipkart; 
public class AutowireingMain { 
 static String path = 
"com/Spring/ByAnnotationAutoWireingConfig/AnnoatationAutowireingAppContext.xml"; 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  ClassPathXmlApplicationContext appcontext = new ClassPathXmlApplicationContext(path); 
  Flipkart flipKart = appcontext.getBean("fpkt", Flipkart.class); 
  String result = flipKart.shopping(new String[] {"Noise Smart Band","Puma","Iphone"}, new 
Float[] 
    {3123.33f,1500.65f,64999.56f}); 
  System.out.println(result); 
 } 
}

Case2 :: Performing Qualifer  Annotation in FlipKart Annotation:- 
@Qualifier is used in Spring to resolve ambiguity when multiple beans of the same type are 
available for autowiring. It tells Spring exactly which bean to inject. 
//Feild level Autowireing 
@Autowired 
@Qualifier("dtdc") 
private Courier courier; 
private Long regNo;

Object

  this.courier = courier; 
  System.out.println("Flipkart:: One Param 
constructor..."); 
 } 
} 
@Autowired 
 public Flipkart(@Qualifier("fFlight") Courier courier) { 
 System.out.println("Flipkart object is created through Constructor:: One param constructor"); 
 this.courier = courier; 
}

//Target Object 
public class Flipkart{ 
@Autowired   //|=> Dependant Object 
  public void setCourier(@Qualifier("bDart") Courier courier) { 
  this.courier = courier; 
  System.out.println("Flipkart.setCourier():: Setter Injection"); 
 } 
} 
@Autowired 
public void setCourier(@Qualifier("dtdc") Courier courier) { 
 System.out.println("Courier object is injected through Setter"); 
 this.courier = courier; 
}

AutoWireing by two Param Constructor: 
@Autowired 
public Flipkart(@Qualifier("bDart") Courier courier,@Value("256") Long regNo) { 
 System.out.println("FlipKart :: Two Param Constructor...!"); 
 this.courier = courier; 
 this.regNo = regNo; 
} 
public long getRegNo() 
{ 
 return regNo; 
}
