Some Important Annotations: 
@Autowired 
  Definition: Marks a constructor, field, or setter method to be autowired by Spring's dependency injection facilities. 
  Why it is used: To inject dependencies automatically. 
  Example: 
    @Autowired 
    private DataSource dataSource; 
@Value 
  Definition: Injects values into fields from properties files or simple expressions. 
  Why it is used: To externalize configuration or use SpEL. 
  Example: 
    @Value("${items.info.idlyPrice}") // Property injection 
    public float idlyPrice; 
    @Value("#{item.idlyPrice+item.dosaPrice}") // SpEL 
    private Float billAmount; 
@Configuration 
  Definition: Indicates that a class declares one or more @Bean methods and may be processed by the Spring 
container to generate bean definitions. 
  Why it is used: For Java-based configuration of beans. 
  Example: 
    @Configuration 
    public class PersistConfig { ... } 
@Bean 
  Definition: Indicates that a method produces a bean to be managed by the Spring container. 
  Why it is used: To manually create and configure items, especially from third-party libraries (like DataSources). 
  Example: 
    @Bean 
    public ComboPooledDataSource createDS() { ... } 
@ImportResource 
  Definition: Indicates that an XML configuration file should be imported. 
  Why it is used: To load legacy XML configuration in a Spring Boot application. 
  Example: 
    @ImportResource(locations = "in/ineuron/cfg/applicationContext.xml") 
JSR-330 (Java Standard) Annotations ----------------------------------- 
(These are standard Java annotations used as alternatives to Spring annotations.) 
@Named 
  Definition: Standard equivalent to @Component (and @Qualifier). 
  Why it is used: To define a named bean in a portable, non-framework-specific way. 
  Example: 
    @Named("std") 
    public class Student { ... } 
@Inject 
  Definition: Standard equivalent to @Autowired. 
  Why it is used: To perform dependency injection in a portable way. 
  Example: 
    @Inject 
    @Named(value="courseId") 
    private ICourseMaterial material; 
JSR-250 (Java Lifecycle) Annotations ------------------------------------ 
(Standard Java annotations for Bean Lifecycle management.) 
@PostConstruct 
  Definition: Marks a method to be executed after the bean has been instantiated and all dependency 
injection has been completed. 
  Why it is used: To perform initialization logic that depends on injected dependencies (e.g., 
verifying DB connection, loading cache data) which cannot be done in the constructor. 
  Example: 
    @PostConstruct 
    public void init() { 
        // This runs after 'dataSource' is injected 
        System.out.println("Bean initialized, connection valid: " + (dataSource != null)); 
    } 
@PreDestroy 
  Definition: Marks a method to be executed just before the bean is removed from the Spring 
container. 
  Why it is used: To perform cleanup operations (e.g., closing open files, releasing network 
connections, stopping background threads). 
  Example: 
    @PreDestroy 
    public void cleanup() { 
        System.out.println("Closing resources..."); 
    } 
Project 08: BootProj08-RealTimeDIUsingYML-ExcludingHikariCPConfig ----------------------------------------------------------------- 
Purpose:  
To demonstrate how to exclude the default connection pool (HikariCP) and configure an alternative one (like Apache DBCP2 
or Tomcat JDBC) using "application.yml". 
Flow: 
1. POM Configuration: 
   - Excludes HikariCP from "spring-boot-starter-jdbc". 
   - Adds dependencies for "commons-dbcp2" and "tomcat-jdbc". 
2. Configuration: 
   - "application.yml" provides DataSource properties 
 (url, username, password). 
   - Spring Boot AutoConfiguration detects the available  
Connection Pool libraries and configures one  
(Priority: Hikari -> Tomcat -> DBCP2). 
3. Execution: 
   - EmployeeDaoImpl injects the DataSource. 
   - It prints the class name of the injected DataSource to verify which pool is being used (likely 
org.apache.tomcat.jdbc.pool.DataSource due to priority). 
Real Scenario: 
In enterprise environments, a specific Connection Pool might be mandated due to monitoring tools, compliance, or legacy 
support. This shows how to swap the default HikariCP without changing code logic. --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- 
Project 09: BootProj09-RealTimeDIUsingYML-ManualDataSourceInjection ------------------------------------------------------------------- 
Purpose:  
To demonstrate manual creation of a DataSource bean, overriding Spring Boot's AutoConfiguration. This is useful when you 
need full control over the bean creation (e.g., using C3P0). 
Flow: 
1. Main Class: BootProj09RealTimeDIManualDataSourceApplication 
   - Excludes DataSourceAutoConfiguration and JdbcTemplateAutoConfiguration to prevent Spring from creating a default 
DataSource. 
2. Configuration Class: PersistConfig 
   - Annotated with @Configuration. 
   - Define a @Bean method createDS(). 
   - Manually instantiates ComboPooledDataSource (C3P0), sets properties from Environment, and returns it. 
3. Execution: 
   - The EmployeeDaoImpl receives this manually created C3P0 DataSource. 
Real Scenario: 
Useful when you need to use a specific DataSource implementation not supported by default AutoConfiguration, or when you 
need complex configuration logic (e.g., fetching credentials from a vault) during bean creation. 
<dependency> 
            <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId> 
            <artifactId>spring-boot-starter
jdbc</artifactId> 
            <exclusions> 
                <exclusion> 
                    <groupId>com.zaxxer</groupId> 
                    <artifactId>HikariCP</artifactId> 
                </exclusion> 
            </exclusions> 
        </dependency> 
public class PersistConfig { 
    @Autowired 
    private Environment env; 
    @Bean 
    public ComboPooledDataSource createDS() throws Exception { 
        System.out.println("PersistConfig.createDS()"); 
        ComboPooledDataSource dataSource = new ComboPooledDataSource(); 
        dataSource.setJdbcUrl(env.getProperty("spring.datasource.url")); 
        dataSource.setUser(env.getProperty("spring.datasource.username")); 
        dataSource.setPassword(env.getProperty("spring.datasource.password")); 
        return dataSource; 
    } 
} 
Project 10: BootProj10-UsageofSpel-@ValueAnnotation --------------------------------------------------- 
Purpose:  
To demonstrate the usage of Spring Expression Language (SpEL) and the @Value annotation for injecting values and 
performing dynamic computations. 
Flow: 
1. Components: 
   - ItemsInfo: Holds prices injected from "application.properties" using @Value("${key}"). 
   - BillGenerator: Calculates total bill using SpEL @Value("#{expression}"). 
2. Logic: 
   - #{item.idlyPrice + item.dosaPrice ...}: Dynamically accesses another bean ("item") and performs arithmetic. 
3. Execution: 
   - Main class retrieves BillGenerator and prints the calculated bill. 
Real Scenario: 
Used for dynamic property injection, feature toggles, or calculating values at runtime based on other beans' states (e.g., 
calculating tax based on a configured rate). 
package in.ineuron.comp; 
import 
org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Value; 
import org.springframework.stereotype.Component; 
import in.ineuron.dependent.ItemsInfo; 
@Component("bill") 
public class BillGenerator { 
    @Value("#{item.idlyPrice+item.dosaPrice+item.vadaPrice}") 
    private Float billAmount; 
    @Value("Accord") 
    private String hotelName; 
    @Autowired 
    private ItemsInfo info; 
    @Override 
    public String toString() { 
        return "BillGenerator [billAmount=" + billAmount + ", 
hotelName=" + hotelName + ", info=" + info + "]"; 
    } 
} 
package in.ineuron.dependent; 
import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Value; 
import org.springframework.stereotype.Component; 
@Component("item") 
public class ItemsInfo { 
    @Value("${items.info.idlyPrice}") 
    public float idlyPrice; 
    @Value("${items.info.dosaPrice}") 
    public float dosaPrice; 
    @Value("${items.info.vadaPrice}") 
    public float vadaPrice; 
    @Override 
    public String toString() { 
        return "ItemsInfo [idlyPrice=" + idlyPrice + ", dosaPrice=" + dosaPrice + ", 
vadaPrice=" + vadaPrice + "]"; 
    } 
} 
 package in.ineuron;

@SpringBootApplication 
public class BootProj10UsageOfSpELApplication { 
    public static void main(String[] args) throws Exception { 
        ApplicationContext context = SpringApplication 
                .run(BootProj10UsageOfSpELApplication.class, args); 
        System.out.println("Beans info are :: " + 
Arrays.toString(context.getBeanDefinitionNames()));

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
PROJECT 07: BootProj07-DependancyInjection-JavaConfiguration
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
PURPOSE:
  Demonstrate Non-Invasive DI using JSR-330 (Java Standard) annotations
  instead of Spring-specific ones. Also shows how to integrate legacy XML config.
KEY DEPENDENCY (pom.xml):
  <dependency>
    <groupId>javax.inject</groupId>
    <artifactId>javax.inject</artifactId>
    <version>1</version>
  </dependency>
FILES + ROLES:
  ┌─ BootProj07DependencyInjectionJavaConfigurationApplication.java
  │    @SpringBootApplication
  │    @ImportResource(locations = "in/ineuron/cfg/applicationContext.xml")
  │    → Loads XML config to dynamically alias bean names.
  │    → Retrieves Student bean and calls preparation().
  │
  ├─ Student.java  [in.ineuron.comp]
  │    @Named("std")                    ← JSR-330 equivalent of @Component
  │    @Inject @Named(value="courseId") ← Inject the aliased bean same as like @Autowireing
  │    private ICourseMaterial material;
  │    → Shows field-level injection using standard annotations.
  │
  ├─ ICourseMaterial.java  [in.ineuron.dependent]
  │    public interface ICourseMaterial {
  │        String courseContent();
  │        double price();
  │    }
  │    → Contract interface enabling Strategy Pattern.
  │
  ├─ JavaCourseMaterial.java  [in.ineuron.dependent]
  │    @Named("java")
  │    public final class JavaCourseMaterial implements ICourseMaterial {
  │        courseContent() → "1. oops 2. ExceptionHandling 3.Collection"
  │        price()         → 500
  │    }
  │
  ├─ DotNetCourseMaterial.java  [in.ineuron.dependent]
  │    @Named("dotNet")  ← alternate implementation
  │
  ├─ applicationContext.xml  [in/ineuron/cfg/]
  │    <alias name="${course.choose}" alias="courseId" />
  │    → Reads property and creates alias. Enables runtime switch of implementation.
  │
  └─ application.properties
       course.choose=java   ← Change to "dotNet" to swap implementation!
EXECUTION FLOW:
  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │  1. App starts → @SpringBootApplication triggers ComponentScan          │
  │  2. @ImportResource loads applicationContext.xml                        │
  │  3. XML reads course.choose=java → creates alias "courseId" = "java"   │
  │  4. IOC instantiates JavaCourseMaterial as bean named "java"            │
  │  5. IOC instantiates Student, injects bean "courseId" (=java impl)      │
  │  6. Main retrieves Student → calls preparation() → calls material APIs  │
  │  7. context.close() → @PreDestroy hooks fire → Beans cleaned up         │
  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
DESIGN PATTERNS:
  • Strategy Pattern → ICourseMaterial with Java/DotNet implementations
  • Dependency Injection → via JSR-330 @Inject / @Named
  • Factory Pattern → Spring IOC as Object Factory
CLASS NOTE MAPPING (Class_note_5_April.txt Lines 1–46):
  ✔ Non-Invasive Programming      → @Named / @Inject used instead of @Component / @Autowired
  ✔ @Named for ambiguity           → Student uses @Named(value="courseId") to pick specific impl
  ✔ @Resource vs @Inject           → @Resource cannot be at constructor level; @Inject can
  ✔ Annotation Preference Order    → Java Config > Spring Annotations > Third-party > Custom
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
PROJECT 08: BootProj08-RealTimeDIUsingYML-ExcludingHikariCPConfig
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
PURPOSE:
  Demonstrate swapping the default HikariCP connection pool with an alternative
  (Apache DBCP2 or Tomcat JDBC) by excluding it from the starter dependency.
KEY DEPENDENCIES (pom.xml):
  spring-boot-starter-jdbc  [HikariCP EXCLUDED via <exclusion>]
  commons-dbcp2             [Apache DBCP2]
  tomcat-jdbc               [Tomcat JDBC pool]
  mysql-connector-j         [scope=runtime]
FILES + ROLES:
  ┌─ BootProj08RealTimeDIUsingYMLApplication.java
  │    @SpringBootApplication  ← AutoConfiguration ACTIVE (no exclude)
  │    → Retrieves IEmployeeDAO bean → fetchs employees → prints list
  │
  ├─ EmployeeDaoImpl.java  [in.ineuron.comp]
  │    @Repository
  │    @Autowired DataSource dataSource;   ← Auto-injected by Spring
  │    → Prints: dataSource.getClass().getName() to verify pool type
  │    → Uses try-with-resources for Connection, PreparedStatement, ResultSet
  │    → Maps ResultSet rows to Employee DTO objects
  │
  ├─ IEmployeeDAO.java  [interface]
  │    List<Employee> findAllEmployees() throws Exception;
  │
  ├─ Employee.java  [in.ineuron.dto]
  │    POJO: eid, ename, eage, eaddress + getters/setters/toString
  │
  └─ application.yml
       spring:
         datasource:
           url: jdbc:mysql:///enterprisejavabatch
           username: root
           password: root123
EXECUTION FLOW:
  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │  1. Classpath checked: HikariCP ABSENT (excluded), Tomcat JDBC PRESENT  │
  │  2. AutoConfiguration picks: Tomcat JDBC (2nd priority)                 │
  │  3. DataSource bean created using application.yml properties            │
  │  4. EmployeeDaoImpl @Autowired with Tomcat DataSource                  │
  │  5. findAllEmployees() opens connection → executes SELECT → maps rows   │
  │  6. Output: DataSource Connection is :: org.apache.tomcat.jdbc.pool.DS  │
  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
DataSource AutoConfiguration Priority (CRITICAL for interviews):
  Priority    Pool            Condition
  ───────     ────            ─────────
  1st         HikariCP        Always (when present on classpath)
  2nd         Tomcat JDBC     When HikariCP missing
  3rd         DBCP2           When both above missing
CLASS NOTE MAPPING (Lines 49–96):
  ✔ Hikari exclusion technique         → <exclusions><exclusion>HikariCP</exclusion>
  ✔ DBCP2 / Tomcat alternatives        → Both added as dependencies in pom.xml
  ✔ AutoConfiguration priority order   → Confirmed by class notes lines 56-60

PROJECT 09: BootProj09-RealTimeDIUsingYML-ManualDataSourceInjection
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
PURPOSE:
  Fully disable Spring Boot's DataSource AutoConfiguration and manually create
  a C3P0 ComboPooledDataSource via a @Configuration class.
KEY DEPENDENCIES (pom.xml):
  spring-boot-starter-jdbc  [HikariCP EXCLUDED]
  c3p0:0.9.5.4              [Manual connection pool]
  mysql-connector-j         [runtime]
FILES + ROLES:
  ┌─ BootProj09RealTimeDIManualDataSourceApplication.java
  │    @SpringBootApplication(exclude = {
  │        DataSourceAutoConfiguration.class,
  │        JdbcTemplateAutoConfiguration.class
  │    })
  │    → Tells Spring: "DON'T create any DataSource automatically."
  │    → Retrieves DAO and fetches employees list.
  │
  ├─ PersistConfig.java  [in.ineuron.persist]
  │    @Configuration
  │    public class PersistConfig {
  │        @Autowired
  │        private Environment env;       ← Reads from application.yml
  │
  │        @Bean
  │        public ComboPooledDataSource createDS() throws Exception {
  │            ComboPooledDataSource ds = new ComboPooledDataSource();
  │            ds.setJdbcUrl(env.getProperty("spring.datasource.url"));
  │            ds.setUser(env.getProperty("spring.datasource.username"));
  │            ds.setPassword(env.getProperty("spring.datasource.password"));
  │            return ds;  ← Spring registers this as DataSource bean
  │        }
  │    }
  │
  ├─ EmployeeDaoImpl.java  [same as Proj08 — @Autowired DataSource]
  └─ application.yml       [same properties as Proj08]
EXECUTION FLOW:
  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │  1. @SpringBootApplication(exclude=...) → AutoConfig DISABLED for DS   │
  │  2. Spring scans @Configuration → finds PersistConfig                  │
  │  3. Calls createDS() → Instantiates C3P0 ComboPooledDataSource         │
  │  4. Properties read from Environment (application.yml)                  │
  │  5. C3P0 DataSource registered as Spring Bean                          │
  │  6. EmployeeDaoImpl @Autowired → gets C3P0 DataSource                  │
  │  7. findAllEmployees() → SELECT query via C3P0 connection               │
  │  Output: DataSource :: com.mchange.v2.c3p0.ComboPooledDataSource        │
  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

  ✔ application.yml usage                   → datasource URL, username, password

PROJECT 10: BootProj10-UsageofSpel-@ValueAnnotation
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
PURPOSE:
  Demonstrate two major uses of @Value:
    a) Property injection using ${key}
    b) Spring Expression Language (SpEL) using #{expression} for cross-bean computation
FILES + ROLES:
  ┌─ ItemsInfo.java  [in.ineuron.dependent]
  │    @Component("item")
  │    public class ItemsInfo {
  │        @Value("${items.info.idlyPrice}")  public float idlyPrice;   // = 10
  │        @Value("${items.info.dosaPrice}")  public float dosaPrice;   // = 20
  │        @Value("${items.info.vadaPrice}")  public float vadaPrice;   // = 30
  │    }
  │    → Bean name is "item" — referenced by SpEL in BillGenerator
  │
  ├─ BillGenerator.java  [in.ineuron.comp]
  │    @Component("bill")
  │    public class BillGenerator {
  │        @Value("#{item.idlyPrice + item.dosaPrice + item.vadaPrice}")
  │        private Float billAmount;         // SpEL cross-bean access = 60.0
  │
  │        @Value("Accord")
  │        private String hotelName;         // Literal string injection
  │
  │        @Autowired
  │        private ItemsInfo info;           // Full object injection for display
  │    }
  │
  ├─ application.properties
  │    items.info.idlyPrice= 10
  │    items.info.dosaPrice= 20
  │    items.info.vadaPrice= 30
  │
  └─ BootProj10UsageOfSpELApplication.java
       → Retrieves BillGenerator bean → prints it
       → Output: BillGenerator [billAmount=60.0, hotelName=Accord, info=...]
@Value SYNTAX COMPARISON:
  Syntax                      Purpose                           Example
  ───────────────────         ───────────────────────────────   ─────────────────────────
  @Value("literal")           Inject a fixed/constant value     @Value("Accord")
  @Value("${property.key}")   Read from application.properties  @Value("${idlyPrice}")
  @Value("#{expression}")     SpEL: runtime computation         @Value("#{item.price*2}")
  @Value("#{bean.field}")     SpEL: cross-bean field access     @Value("#{item.idlyPrice}")
SpEL EXECUTION MECHANISM:
  1. Spring loads ItemsInfo bean with name "item"
  2. Properties injected from application.properties
  3. Spring processes @Value("#{item.idlyPrice + ...}") on BillGenerator
  4. SpEL evaluator: fetches "item" bean from context, reads public fields, adds
  5. Result (60.0) injected into BillGenerator.billAmount at startup
CLASS NOTE MAPPING (Lines 162–226):
  ✔ @Value literal            → @Value("Accord") in hotelName
  ✔ @Value property injection → @Value("${idlyPrice}") in ItemsInfo
  ✔ SpEL computation          → @Value("#{item.idlyPrice+...}") in BillGenerator
  ✔ Bean name reference in SpEL→ "item" matches @Component("item") on ItemsInfo

PROJECT Hibernate-01: Core Hibernate — Get Record by ID
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
PURPOSE:
  Demonstrate Core Hibernate (without Spring) for fetching a record from a MySQL
  database by primary key. Shows SessionFactory setup, Session management,
  Entity mapping, and the Singleton utility pattern.
KEY DEPENDENCIES (pom.xml):
  hibernate-core:5.6.15.Final
  mysql-connector-j:8.0.32
  junit:4.11
FILES + ROLES:
  ┌─ hibernate.cfg.xml  [src/main/resources]
  │    <session-factory>
  │      <property name="hibernate.connection.driver_class">
  │          com.mysql.cj.jdbc.Driver</property>
  │      <property name="hibernate.connection.url">
  │          jdbc:mysql:///octbatch</property>
  │      <property name="hibernate.connection.username">root</property>
  │      <property name="hibernate.connection.password">root123</property>
  │      <property name="hibernate.dialect">MySQL8Dialect</property>
  │      <property name="hibernate.show_sql">true</property>
  │      <property name="hibernate.format_sql">true</property>
  │      <property name="hibernate.hbm2ddl.auto">update</property>
  │    </session-factory>
  │
  ├─ Student.java  [in.pwskills.model]
  │    @Entity
  │    public class Student {
  │        @Id
  │        @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
  │        private Integer sid;
  │        private String sname, saddress;
  │        private Integer sage;
  │    }
  │    → @Entity: Maps class to DB table STUDENT
  │    → @Id: Primary key
  │    → @GeneratedValue: Auto-increment by DB
  │
  ├─ HibernateUtil.java  [in.pwskills.util]
  │    public class HibernateUtil {                     ← Utility class
  │        private static SessionFactory sessionFactory; ← Singleton
  │        private HibernateUtil() {}                   ← Private constructor
  │
  │        static {
  │            sessionFactory = new Configuration()
  │                .configure()                         ← Reads hibernate.cfg.xml
  │                .addAnnotatedClass(Student.class)    ← Register @Entity class
  │                .buildSessionFactory();              ← Creates the factory
  │        }
  │
  │        public static Session getSession() {
  │            if (session == null)
  │                session = sessionFactory.openSession();
  │            return session;
  │        }
  │    }
  │
  └─ GetRecordApp.java  [in.pwskills]
       Session session = HibernateUtil.getSession();
       Student student = session.get(Student.class, id);  ← Fetch by PK
       → Handles HibernateException and general Exception
       → finally block: closeSession(), closeSessionFactory()
EXECUTION FLOW:
  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │  1. Static block in HibernateUtil fires at class loading                │
  │  2. Configuration().configure() reads hibernate.cfg.xml                │
  │  3. addAnnotatedClass(Student.class) — register entity                 │
  │  4. buildSessionFactory() — heavyweight object, created ONCE            │
  │  5. GetRecordApp.main() → getSession() → session.get(Student, 99)      │
  │  6. Hibernate generates: SELECT * FROM STUDENT WHERE SID=99            │
  │  7. ResultSet mapped to Student object via reflection (zero-arg ctor)  │
  │  8. Print student → finally: disconnects session + factory             │
  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
JPA ANNOTATIONS REFERENCE:
  @Entity              → Marks class as persistent (maps to table)
  @Id                  → Marks primary key field
  @GeneratedValue      → Auto-generate PK values
  GenerationType.IDENTITY → Delegates to DB auto_increment
  GenerationType.AUTO     → Hibernate decides strategy
  GenerationType.SEQUENCE → Uses DB sequence object
  GenerationType.TABLE    → Hibernate uses separate table for PK generation
HIBERNATE KEY PROPERTIES EXPLAINED:
  Property                  Value           Meaning
  ─────────────────         ─────────       ─────────────────────────────────
  show_sql                  true            Prints Hibernate SQL to console
  format_sql                true            Formats SQL for readability
  hbm2ddl.auto             update           Creates/alters table at startup
  hibernate.dialect         MySQL8Dialect   Generates MySQL-compatible SQL

PROJECT Hibernate-02: Maven Inheritance Demonstration
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
PURPOSE:
  Demonstrate Maven's <parent> mechanism: Child project inherits all
  dependencies and properties from a parent pom.
CONFIGURATION (pom.xml — child):
  <parent>
    <groupId>pwskills</groupId>
    <artifactId>Hibernate-01</artifactId>
    <version>1.1</version>
  </parent>
EFFECT:
  Hibernate-02 inherits:
  → hibernate-core:5.6.15.Final  (no need to re-declare)
  → mysql-connector-j:8.0.32     (inherited)
  → Properties: hibernate-version, mysql-version, compiler settings
WHY USE IT:
  Enterprise multi-module projects share common dependencies from a parent BOM.
  Spring Boot itself uses this: spring-boot-starter-parent is the parent POM.
CLASS NOTE MAPPING (Lines 840–887):
  ✔ Maven Inheritance concept     → <parent> tag in Hibernate-02 pom.xml
  ✔ Inheriting deps + properties  → Hibernate-02 needs only its own deps

  </dependency>
  → Centralizes version management. Change once → applies everywhere.
Maven Feature: Exclusion (from class notes Lines 756–769):
  <dependency>
    <groupId>org.hibernate</groupId>
    <artifactId>hibernate-core</artifactId>
    <version>5.6.15.Final</version>
    <exclusions>
      <exclusion>
        <groupId>org.jboss.logging</groupId>
        <artifactId>jboss-logging</artifactId>
      </exclusion>
    </exclusions>
  </dependency>
  → Use when a transitive dependency conflicts with your own logger (e.g., SLF4J).

SECTION 6: ALL ANNOTATIONS REFERENCE CARD
================================================================================
 ANNOTATION              | PACKAGE       | PURPOSE
 ────────────────────────+───────────────+──────────────────────────────────────────
 @SpringBootApplication  | springframework| Combines @Config+@EnableAutoConfig+@Scan
 @Component              | springframework| Register a class as a Spring Bean
 @Repository             | springframework| DAO component; enables Persistence exception tx
 @Configuration          | springframework| Class holds @Bean definitions
 @Bean                   | springframework| Method produces a Bean for Spring context
 @Autowired              | springframework| Inject a dependency (field/constructor/setter)
 @Value                  | springframework| Inject a property value or SpEL expression
 @ImportResource         | springframework| Load legacy XML Spring config file
 @Named                  | javax.inject  | JSR-330: Bean name + replaces @Component
 @Inject                 | javax.inject  | JSR-330: DI (field/constructor/setter)
 @Resource               | javax.annotation| JSR-250: DI (field/setter only)
 @PostConstruct          | javax.annotation| JSR-250: Init method after DI complete
 @PreDestroy             | javax.annotation| JSR-250: Cleanup before bean destroyed
 @Entity                 | javax.persistence| JPA: Map class to DB table
 @Id                     | javax.persistence| JPA: Mark primary key field
 @GeneratedValue         | javax.persistence| JPA: Auto-generate PK
================================================================================
SECTION 7: KEY INTERVIEW QUESTIONS — BASIC TO ADVANCED
================================================================================
────────────────────────────
  BASIC
────────────────────────────
Q1) What is Dependency Injection? What are its types?
A:  Dependency Injection is a design pattern where object dependencies are
    provided by an external container (Spring IOC) rather than the class itself.
    Types: (a) Constructor Injection, (b) Setter Injection, (c) Field Injection.
Q2) What is the difference between @Component, @Service, @Repository, @Controller?
A:  All are specializations of @Component (same function: register a Bean).
    - @Repository: DAO layer; enables persistence exception translation.
    - @Service: Business logic layer (no extra behavior currently).
    - @Controller: Web layer; handles HTTP requests.
Q3) What does @SpringBootApplication do?
A:  It is a meta-annotation combining:
    - @Configuration (Java-based config)
    - @EnableAutoConfiguration (auto-setup based on classpath)
    - @ComponentScan (scans current package and sub-packages for beans)
Q4) What is the difference between application.properties and application.yml?
A:  Both hold configuration. .yml uses a hierarchical/YAML structure (more
    readable for nested configs). .properties uses flat key=value pairs.
Q5) What is HikariCP?
A:  HikariCP is the default JDBC connection pool used by Spring Boot 2.5+.
    It is chosen for its high performance and low overhead.
────────────────────────────
  INTERMEDIATE
────────────────────────────
Q6) How do you switch the DataSource from HikariCP to Apache DBCP2?
A:  Step 1: Exclude HikariCP from spring-boot-starter-jdbc in pom.xml.
    Step 2: Add commons-dbcp2 dependency.
    Spring Boot AutoConfiguration detects DBCP2 on classpath and configures it.
Q7) What is the difference between @Autowired and @Inject?
A:  @Autowired is Spring-specific; @Inject is JSR-330 (Java standard).
    @Autowired has a "required" attribute (defaults to true).
    @Inject does not have a "required" equivalent — use @Nullable instead.
Q8) How do you disable a specific AutoConfiguration in Spring Boot?
A:  Use the exclude attribute:
    @SpringBootApplication(exclude = { DataSourceAutoConfiguration.class })
Q9) What is Spring Expression Language (SpEL)?
A:  SpEL is a powerful scripting language built into Spring. It allows:
    - Accessing bean properties: #{beanName.property}
    - Arithmetic:               #{item.price * 1.18}
    - String manipulation, conditionals, method calls.
    Used via @Value annotation at field injection time.
Q10) What is the difference between @Named and @Qualifier?
A:  @Named is JSR-330; @Qualifier is Spring-specific. Both resolve ambiguity
    when multiple beans of the same type exist. @Named also replaces @Component.
Q11) What is @ImportResource used for?
A:  To import legacy Spring XML bean configuration files into a Spring Boot app.
    Useful when migrating from XML-based Spring to annotation-based Spring Boot.
────────────────────────────
  ADVANCED
────────────────────────────
Q12) Explain the DataSource AutoConfiguration priority in Spring Boot 2.5+.
A:  Spring Boot checks the classpath in this order:
    1. HikariCP (if zaxxer.HikariCP jar is present)
    2. Tomcat JDBC (if tomcat-jdbc jar is present and HikariCP absent)
    3. Apache DBCP2 (fallback if both above are absent)
    The first found pool is configured automatically using application.yml props.
Q13) How does SpEL cross-bean computation work at runtime?
A:  When Spring processes @Value("#{item.idlyPrice + item.dosaPrice}"):
    1. Locates the "item" bean in the ApplicationContext.
    2. Reads public field idlyPrice (which was already injected from properties).
    3. Evaluates the arithmetic expression at field-injection time.
    4. Assigns result to the annotated field.
    This happens during the BeanPostProcessor phase of bean lifecycle.
Q14) What is Maven Inheritance? How is it used?
A:  A child project's pom.xml can declare a <parent> tag pointing to a parent
    project's groupId, artifactId, version. The child inherits all dependencies,
    plugins, and properties from the parent. Used in multi-module projects to
    avoid duplicating dependency declarations (like Spring Boot's parent pom).
Q15) Explain the Singleton pattern in HibernateUtil.
A:  HibernateUtil uses a static field (SessionFactory) initialized in a static
    block. The private constructor prevents external instantiation. This ensures
    only ONE SessionFactory is created for the entire application lifetime.
    SessionFactory is heavyweight — creating it repeatedly is expensive.
Q16) What is the lifecycle difference between SessionFactory and Session?
A:  - SessionFactory: Created ONCE per application. Heavyweight. Thread-safe.
    - Session: Created PER UNIT OF WORK / transaction. Lightweight. Not thread-safe.
    Use HibernateUtil to share one SessionFactory but open fresh Sessions per operation.
Q17) How do you install a non-Central jar (e.g., Oracle JDBC) for Maven use?
A:  Use the Maven install plugin:
    mvn install:install-file -Dfile=<path/to/jar>
      -DgroupId=<group> -DartifactId=<artifact>
      -Dversion=<ver> -Dpackaging=jar
    This installs the jar to the local .m2 repository. Reference it in pom.xml
    normally. Other developers need to run the same install command.
Q18) What is Non-Invasive programming? Why is it preferred?
A:  Non-Invasive means your business classes do not import or depend on
    framework-specific APIs. Using JSR-330 (@Named, @Inject) instead of Spring's
    (@Component, @Autowired) means the same class could theoretically work with
    another IoC container (e.g., Guice) without modification. This improves
    portability and testability.
================================================================================
SECTION 8: EXECUTION FLOW DIAGRAMS
================================================================================
[ Spring Boot DI Flow — BootProj07 ]
  APP START
    │
    ├─→ @SpringBootApplication triggers ComponentScan
    │       └─→ Finds @Named("java"), @Named("dotNet"), @Named("std") beans
    │
    ├─→ @ImportResource loads applicationContext.xml
    │       └─→ <alias name="${course.choose}" alias="courseId"/>
    │               └─→ reads course.choose=java → alias "courseId" → "java" bean
    │
    ├─→ IOC Container: Instantiate JavaCourseMaterial (bean "java")
    ├─→ IOC Container: Instantiate Student (bean "std")
    │       └─→ @Inject @Named("courseId") → inject JavaCourseMaterial
    │
    └─→ main() → context.getBean(Student.class)
                  └─→ student.preparation()
                          └─→ material.courseContent() + material.price()
                               → "1. oops 2. Exception Handling 3. Collection"
[ Spring Boot DataSource Flow — BootProj08 & 09 ]
  [Proj08 — AutoConfig]                [Proj09 — Manual Bean]
  ────────────────────────             ──────────────────────────────────
  @SpringBootApplication               @SpringBootApplication(exclude=DataSource)
         │                                     │
  Classpath check:                     ComponentScan → PersistConfig found
  HikariCP absent →                            │
  Tomcat JDBC present →                @Bean createDS() called
  AutoConfig → TomcatDataSource                │
  created from application.yml         → new ComboPooledDataSource()
         │                             → setJdbcUrl(env.getProperty(...))
  @Autowired DataSource in DAO         → registered as DataSource bean
         │                                     │
  findAllEmployees() → JDBC queries    findAllEmployees() → JDBC queries
[ SpEL Flow — BootProj10 ]
  App Start → Scan → ItemsInfo("item") created
                  │
                  └─→ @Value("${idlyPrice}") = 10
                      @Value("${dosaPrice}") = 20
                      @Value("${vadaPrice}") = 30
                  │
  BillGenerator("bill") created
    │
    ├─→ @Value("#{item.idlyPrice+item.dosaPrice+item.vadaPrice}")
    │       → SpEL evaluator: lookup "item" bean → read fields → sum = 60.0
    ├─→ @Value("Accord") → literal string injection
    └─→ @Autowired ItemsInfo → full bean injected
    │
  main() → getBean(BillGenerator) → System.out.println()
    → Output: BillGenerator [billAmount=60.0, hotelName=Accord, info=...]

SECTION 9: MAVEN COMPLETE REFERENCE
================================================================================
[ Maven Repositories ]
  1. LOCAL   → ~/.m2/repository  — cached/installed jars on dev machine
  2. CENTRAL → https://repo.maven.apache.org  — official Maven repo
  3. REMOTE  → Custom org URLs (e.g., JFrog Artifactory):
               <repositories>
                 <repository>
                   <id>sample</id>
                   <url>https://broadinstitute.jfrog.io/</url>
                 </repository>
               </repositories>
[ Maven Build Lifecycle Phases ]
  validate → compile → test → package → verify → install → deploy
[ Maven Commands Quick Reference ]
  mvn compile           → Compiles source code
  mvn test              → Runs tests
  mvn package           → Creates JAR/WAR
  mvn install           → Installs to local repo
  mvn exec:java         → Runs mainClass via exec plugin
  mvn install:install-file → Installs external jar to local .m2
[ Maven Archetype — Create Project from CLI ]
  mvn archetype:generate
    -DgroupId=ineuron
    -DartifactId=SwapDemoApp
    -DarchetypeArtifactId=maven-archetype-quickstart
    -Dpackage=in.ineuron
    -Dversion=1.0
    -DinteractiveMode=false

SECTION 10: QUICK REVISION SUMMARY
================================================================================
○ DEPENDENCY INJECTION:
  · @Inject (JSR-330) = @Autowired (Spring). @Named (JSR-330) = @Component (Spring)
  · Annotation order: JSR-330 > Spring > Third-party > Custom
  · @Resource = field/setter only. @Inject = field/constructor/setter.
○ DATASOURCE:
  · Default pool: HikariCP. Priority: Hikari < Tomcat < DBCP2 (when excluded).
  · Exclude via: <exclusion> in spring-boot-starter-jdbc dependency.
  · Manual: @SpringBootApplication(exclude=DataSourceAutoConfig) + @Bean method.
○ SPEL:
  · ${key} = property file value.  #{expr} = SpEL runtime expression.
  · Can access other beans: #{beanName.field}. Evaluated at DI time.
○ HIBERNATE:
  · hibernate.cfg.xml: driver, url, username, password, dialect, show_sql, hbm2ddl.
  · hbm2ddl.auto: create | update | validate | create-drop.
  · Session = unit of work.  SessionFactory = application-level singleton.
  · session.get(Entity.class, id) → fetches by PK (returns null if not found).
○ MAVEN:
  · <properties> = declare reusable version variables.
  · <exclusion> = remove a transitive dependency from a jar.
  · <parent> = inherit deps + props from parent pom.
  · Local repo install: mvn install:install-file with -Dfile, -DgroupId etc.
  · exec-maven-plugin: runs main class via mvn package (bind to package phase).
○ IMPORTANT ANNOTATIONS CHECKLIST:
  @SpringBootApplication  @Configuration  @Bean  @Component  @Repository
  @Autowired  @Value  @ImportResource  @Named  @Inject  @Resource
  @PostConstruct  @PreDestroy  @Entity  @Id  @GeneratedValue

SECTION 11: MAVEN INTERNALS — DEPENDENCY DOWNLOAD, BUILD & RUNTIME FLOW
================================================================================
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
11.1  HOW MAVEN RESOLVES DEPENDENCIES — COMPLETE INTERNAL FLOW
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  When you run "mvn package" or import a project in Eclipse/IntelliJ:
  STEP 1: Maven reads pom.xml
  │
  │   pom.xml declares:
  │   <dependency>
  │     <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
  │     <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-jdbc</artifactId>
  │   </dependency>
  │
  ▼
  STEP 2: Maven checks LOCAL REPOSITORY first
  │
  │   Location: C:\Users\<YourName>\.m2\repository\
  │
  │   Path checked:
  │   .m2/repository/org/springframework/boot/spring-boot-starter-jdbc/2.7.10/
  │                └── spring-boot-starter-jdbc-2.7.10.jar  ← exists? USE IT
  │                                                           ← missing?  GO ONLINE
  │
  ▼
  STEP 3: If NOT in local repo → Maven downloads from CENTRAL REPO
  │
  │   URL: https://repo.maven.apache.org/maven2/
  │   OR   custom remote repo (configured via <repositories> in pom.xml)
  │
  │   Download path example:
  │   https://repo1.maven.apache.org/maven2/org/springframework/boot/
  │            spring-boot-starter-jdbc/2.7.10/spring-boot-starter-jdbc-2.7.10.jar
  │
  ▼
  STEP 4: Maven saves downloaded jar to LOCAL REPO (.m2)
  │
  │   Next time the same jar is needed → served from local cache (no internet)
  │
  ▼
  STEP 5: Maven resolves TRANSITIVE DEPENDENCIES
  │
  │   spring-boot-starter-jdbc pulls in:
  │   ├── spring-jdbc
  │   ├── HikariCP        ← (unless excluded!)
  │   └── spring-boot-starter
  │           └── spring-core, spring-beans, spring-context, ...
  │
  │   Maven builds a FULL DEPENDENCY TREE (mvn dependency:tree shows this)
  │
  ▼
  STEP 6: Maven compiles source code (compile phase)
  │   javac src/main/java/**/*.java → target/classes/
  │
  ▼
  STEP 7: Maven runs tests (test phase)
  │   Runs JUnit tests in src/test/java/
  │
  ▼
  STEP 8: Maven packages (package phase)
  │   Creates: target/ProjectName-0.0.1-SNAPSHOT.jar
  │   For Spring Boot: creates FAT JAR (all deps bundled inside)
  │
  ▼
  STEP 9: At RUNTIME — JVM loads classes from JAR
  │
  │   JVM -cp target/ProjectName.jar  ← classpath includes all dep jars
  │   Class Loader loads .class files → method area of JVM
  │   main() method entry point invoked
  │
  └──► APPLICATION STARTS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

  JVM START

    │
    └──► ((ConfigurableApplicationContext)context).close()
              → triggers @PreDestroy methods (if any)
              → Spring destroys all beans → GC
  OBJECT CREATION SEQUENCE (Chronological):
  ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  T0 → JVM starts → main() called
  T1 → Spring IOC Container created
  T2 → new JavaCourseMaterial()   [static block fires first]
  T3 → new DotNetCourseMaterial() [static block fires first]
  T4 → XML alias created: "courseId" = "java"
  T5 → new Student()              [static block fires first]
  T6 → Student.material = JavaCourseMaterial  [DI happens]
  T7 → main() resumes, getBean(), calls methods
  T8 → context.close() → beans destroyed → JVM exits

  JVM START → main()
    │
    ▼
  SpringApplication.run(BootProj08...class, args)
    │
    ├──► AutoConfiguration: spring-boot-starter-jdbc found on classpath
    │         │

    │         │         HikariCP jar? → ABSENT (excluded in pom.xml)
    │         │         tomcat-jdbc?  → PRESENT
    │         │         Result: Tomcat JDBC DataSource selected

    │         │

    │                   → IOC injects TomcatDataSource into EmployeeDaoImpl.dataSource

    │

    │         → returns EmployeeDaoImpl instance
    │

              │
              ├──► Prints: "DataSource Connection is :: org.apache.tomcat.jdbc.pool.DataSource"
              │
              ├──► dataSource.getConnection()
              │         → TomcatDataSource opens JDBC connection to MySQL
              │
              ├──► connection.prepareStatement(SQL_SELECT_QUERY)
              │         → Sends: "select eid,ename,eage,eaddress from employee"
              │
              ├──► pstmt.executeQuery()
              │         → MySQL executes query → returns ResultSet
              │
              ├──► while(resultSet.next())
              │         ──► new Employee()
              │         ──► employee.setEid(resultSet.getInt(1))
              │         ──► employee.setEname(resultSet.getString(2))
              │         ──► employee.setEage(resultSet.getInt(3))
              │         ──► employee.setEaddress(resultSet.getString(4))
              │         ──► empList.add(employee)
              │
              └──► return empList → printed by forEach(System.out::println)

12.4  BootProj10 — SPEL VALUE INJECTION METHOD CALL CHART
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  JVM START → main()
    │
    ▼
  SpringApplication.run(BootProj10UsageOfSpELApplication.class, args)
    │
    ├──► ComponentScan → in.ineuron package
    │
    ├──► PHASE 1: Instantiate + Inject ItemsInfo Bean
    │         │
    │         ├──► new ItemsInfo()   → Java object created
    │         │
    │         ├──► BeanPostProcessor processes @Value annotations:
    │         │
    │         │    @Value("${items.info.idlyPrice}")
    │         │         → reads application.properties
    │         │         → idlyPrice = 10.0  ← INJECTED
    │         │
    │         │    @Value("${items.info.dosaPrice}")
    │         │         → dosaPrice = 20.0  ← INJECTED
    │         │
    │         │    @Value("${items.info.vadaPrice}")
    │         │         → vadaPrice = 30.0  ← INJECTED
    │         │
    │         └──► ItemsInfo bean "item" fully initialized
    │
    ├──► PHASE 2: Instantiate + Inject BillGenerator Bean
    │         │
    │         ├──► new BillGenerator()  → Java object created
    │         │
    │         ├──► @Value("#{item.idlyPrice + item.dosaPrice + item.vadaPrice}")
    │         │         SpEL Engine:
    │         │         Step a: lookup bean named "item" from ApplicationContext
    │         │         Step b: access public field idlyPrice → 10.0
    │         │         Step c: access public field dosaPrice → 20.0
    │         │         Step d: access public field vadaPrice → 30.0
    │         │         Step e: evaluate 10.0 + 20.0 + 30.0 = 60.0
    │         │         Step f: inject 60.0 into billAmount field
    │         │
    │         ├──► @Value("Accord")
    │         │         → literal string "Accord" injected into hotelName
    │         │
    │         └──► @Autowired ItemsInfo info
    │                   → full ItemsInfo bean injected into BillGenerator.info
    │
    ├──► main() resumes
    │
    ├──► context.getBean(BillGenerator.class)
    │         → returns fully initialized BillGenerator
    │
    └──► System.out.println(billGenerator)
              → BillGenerator.toString() called:
              → "BillGenerator [billAmount=60.0, hotelName=Accord,
                 info=ItemsInfo [idlyPrice=10.0, dosaPrice=20.0, vadaPrice=30.0]]"

12.5  Hibernate-01 — COMPLETE METHOD CALL HIERARCHY
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  JVM START
    │
    ▼
  GetRecordApp.main(String[] args)
    │
    ├──► System.out.println(HibernateUtil.getSession())
    │         │
    │         ▼
    │    [HibernateUtil class loads for the first time]
    │         │
    │         ├──► STATIC BLOCK fires:
    │         │         new Configuration()
    │         │               │
    │         │               ├──► .configure()
    │         │               │         reads: src/main/resources/hibernate.cfg.xml
    │         │               │         loads: driver_class, url, username, password
    │         │               │                dialect, show_sql, format_sql, hbm2ddl
    │         │               │
    │         │               ├──► .addAnnotatedClass(Student.class)
    │         │               │         registers Student @Entity
    │         │               │         maps: Student ↔ STUDENT table
    │         │               │
    │         │               └──► .buildSessionFactory()
    │         │                         Creates HEAVY SessionFactory object
    │         │                         (DB schema validated/updated per hbm2ddl=update)
    │         │                         Hibernate generates + logs DDL SQL
    │         │
    │         └──► getSession():
    │                   session == null → sessionFactory.openSession()
    │                   returns Session object (prints its toString)
    │
    ├──► int id = 99
    │
    ├──► session = HibernateUtil.getSession()  ← reuses existing session
    │
    ├──► session.get(Student.class, id)
    │         │
    │         ├──► Hibernate checks 1st-level cache (Session cache)
    │         │         → not found → queries DB
    │         │
    │         ├──► Generates SQL:
    │         │         select student0_.sid as sid1_0_0_,
    │         │                student0_.sage as sage2_0_0_,
    │         │                student0_.saddress as saddres3_0_0_,
    │         │                student0_.sname as sname4_0_0_
    │         │         from STUDENT student0_
    │         │         where student0_.sid=99
    │         │
    │         ├──► Sends SQL to MySQL → receives ResultSet
    │         │
    │         ├──► Student() zero-arg constructor called (by Hibernate via reflection)
    │         │         → "Hibernate uses Zero argument constructor internally"
    │         │
    │         └──► Hibernate sets field values via setters/reflection
    │                   → returns Student object (or null if not found)
    │
    ├──► if(student != null) System.out.println(student)  → Student.toString()
    │
    └──► finally block:
              ├──► HibernateUtil.closeSession(session)
              │         session != null → session.close() → releases JDBC connection
              │
              └──► HibernateUtil.closeSessionFactory()
                        sessionFactory != null → sessionFactory.close()
                        → all connection pools released → JVM exits
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
12.6  MavenProj1 — RAW JDBC METHOD CALL CHART
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  [mvn package] triggers exec-maven-plugin → calls:
    │
    ▼
  JdbcSelectApp.main(String[] args)
    │
    ├──► String url = "jdbc:oracle:thin:@localhost:1521:XE"
    │    String username = "System"
    │    String password = "root123"
    │
    ├──► DriverManager.getConnection(url, username, password)
    │         │
    │         ├──► Oracle JDBC driver loaded from local .m2 repo
    │         │         (previously installed via mvn install:install-file)
    │         │
    │         └──► Establishes TCP connection to Oracle on port 1521
    │                   returns: OracleConnection object
    │
    ├──► connection.createStatement()
    │         → returns Statement object
    │
    ├──► statement.executeQuery("SELECT SID,SNAME,SAGE,SADDR FROM STUDENT")
    │         → Sends SQL to Oracle DB
    │         → returns ResultSet (cursor positioned before first row)
    │
    ├──► while(resultSet.next())
    │         ├── resultSet.getInt(1)     → SID    (Integer)
    │         ├── resultSet.getString(2)  → SNAME  (String)
    │         ├── resultSet.getInt(3)     → SAGE   (Integer)
    │         ├── resultSet.getString(4)  → SADDR  (String)
    │         └── System.out.println(id + "\t" + name + "\t" + age + "\t" + addr)
    │
    └──► connection.close()
              → JDBC connection returned to pool / closed
              → "Closing the connection..."

13.3  MAVEN BUILD MODULE CHART
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  ╔═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗
  ║              MAVEN BUILD PIPELINE                                     ║
  ╠═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╣
  ║                                                                       ║
  ║   pom.xml                                                             ║
  ║     │                                                                  ║
  ║     ├──► <parent>          → inherits from spring-boot-starter-parent ║
  ║     ├──► <properties>      → java.version, spring.version, etc.       ║
  ║     ├──► <dependencies>    → declares needed jars                     ║
  ║     │        └── <exclusion> → removes unwanted transitive deps       ║
  ║     └──► <build><plugins>  → exec-plugin, spring-boot-maven-plugin    ║
  ║                ▼                                                       ║
  ║   MAVEN LIFECYCLE                                                      ║
  ║   ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────┐  ┌─────────┐  ┌────────┐    ║
  ║   │ validate │→ │ compile  │→ │ test │→ │ package │→ │install │    ║
  ║   └──────────┘  └──────────┘  └──────┘  └─────────┘  └────────┘    ║
  ║                      ▲                       │                        ║
  ║                      │ javac                 │ creates FAT JAR        ║
  ║               src/main/java                  ▼                        ║
  ║               ↓  →  →  →  →  →     target/project.jar               ║
  ║             .class files                     │                        ║
  ║             in target/classes                ├── all dep jars INSIDE  ║
  ║                                              └── JVM runs this        ║
  ║                                                                       ║
  ║   DEPENDENCY RESOLUTION FLOW:                                         ║
  ║   pom.xml declares dep → check LOCAL .m2 → if absent → download      ║
  ║   from CENTRAL (maven.apache.org) → save to .m2 → add to classpath   ║
  ╚═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╝
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
13.4  SPEL COMPUTATION CHART (BootProj10)
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  ╔═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗
  ║  SpEL CROSS-BEAN COMPUTATION FLOW                                     ║
  ╠═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╣
  ║                                                                       ║
  ║  application.properties                                               ║
  ║  ┌─────────────────────────────┐                                      ║
  ║  │ items.info.idlyPrice = 10   │                                      ║
  ║  │ items.info.dosaPrice = 20   │                                      ║
  ║  │ items.info.vadaPrice = 30   │                                      ║
  ║  └──────────────┬──────────────┘                                      ║
  ║                 │ @Value("${...}")                                     ║
  ║                 ▼                                                      ║
  ║  ┌─────────────────────────────┐                                      ║
  ║  │  ItemsInfo Bean ("item")    │                                      ║
  ║  │  idlyPrice = 10.0           │                                      ║
  ║  │  dosaPrice = 20.0           │                                      ║
  ║  │  vadaPrice = 30.0           │                                      ║
  ║  └──────────────┬──────────────┘                                      ║
  ║                 │                                                       ║
  ║                 │  SpEL reads "item" bean                              ║
  ║                 │  "#{item.idlyPrice + item.dosaPrice + item.vadaPrice}"║
  ║                 ▼                                                      ║
  ║  ┌─────────────────────────────┐                                      ║
  ║  │  SpEL Evaluation Engine     │                                      ║
  ║  │  10.0 + 20.0 + 30.0 = 60.0 │                                      ║
  ║  └──────────────┬──────────────┘                                      ║
  ║                 │ inject result                                         ║
  ║                 ▼                                                      ║
  ║  ┌─────────────────────────────┐                                      ║
  ║  │  BillGenerator Bean ("bill")│                                      ║
  ║  │  billAmount  = 60.0         │ ← SpEL result                        ║
  ║  │  hotelName   = "Accord"     │ ← literal @Value                     ║
  ║  │  info        = ItemsInfo obj│ ← @Autowired                         ║
  ║  └──────────────┬──────────────┘                                      ║
  ║                 │                                                       ║
  ║                 ▼                                                      ║
  ║  OUTPUT: BillGenerator [billAmount=60.0, hotelName=Accord,            ║
  ║           info=ItemsInfo[idlyPrice=10.0, dosaPrice=20.0, vadaPrice=30.0]]║
  ╚═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╝
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
13.5  DATASOURCE SELECTION DECISION CHART (BootProj08/09)
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  ╔═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗
  ║  DATASOURCE AUTOCONFIGURATION DECISION TREE                           ║
  ╠═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╣
  ║                                                                       ║
  ║  Spring Boot starts                                                   ║
  ║       │                                                               ║
  ║       ▼                                                               ║
  ║  spring-boot-starter-jdbc on classpath?                               ║
  ║       │ YES                    │ NO                                   ║
  ║       │                        └──► No DataSource created             ║
  ║       ▼                                                               ║
  ║  @SpringBootApplication has exclude=DataSourceAutoConfiguration?      ║
  ║       │ YES                    │ NO                                   ║
  ║       │                        │                                      ║
  ║       ▼                        ▼                                      ║
  ║  NO AutoDataSource         HikariCP jar on classpath?                 ║
  ║  → Check @Configuration       │ YES          │ NO                    ║
  ║    for @Bean DataSource        ▼              ▼                       ║
  ║       │              CREATE HikariDS    Tomcat JDBC jar present?      ║
  ║       ▼              (Proj.DEFAULT)         │ YES        │ NO        ║
  ║  C3P0 ComboPooled    ← Proj08 if not        ▼            ▼           ║
  ║  DataSource created    excluded fully  CREATE Tomcat  DBCP2 present?  ║
  ║  (Proj09 approach)                    DataSource     │YES │ NO       ║
  ║                                       (Proj08 flow)  ▼    ▼          ║
  ║                                                    CREATE  ERROR!     ║
  ║                                                    DBCP2   No pool    ║
  ║                                                    DataSrc found      ║
  ╚═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╝

  ╔═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗

  ║  Hibernate-01 (PARENT POM — packaging=pom)                            ║

  ║  │  <groupId>pwskills</groupId>                                   │   ║
  ║  │  <artifactId>Hibernate-01</artifactId>  <version>1.1</version>│   ║

  ║  │  </properties>                                                 │   ║
  ║  │  <dependencies>                                                │   ║
  ║  │    hibernate-core, mysql-connector-j, junit                   │   ║
  ║  │  </dependencies>                                               │   ║
  ║  └────────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────┘   ║
  ║                               │  INHERITANCE (like Java extends)      ║
  ║                               ▼                                        ║
  ║  Hibernate-02 (CHILD POM)                                             ║
  ║  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   ║
  ║  │  <parent>                                                      │   ║
  ║  │    <groupId>pwskills</groupId>                                 │   ║
  ║  │    <artifactId>Hibernate-01</artifactId>                       │   ║
  ║  │    <version>1.1</version>                                      │   ║
  ║  │  </parent>                                                     │   ║
  ║  │                                                                │   ║
  ║  │  INHERITS: hibernate-core ✔  mysql-connector-j ✔  junit ✔    │   ║
  ║  │            hibernate-version property ✔                        │   ║
  ║  │                                                                │   ║
  ║  │  CHILD can OVERRIDE or ADD its own extra deps                  │   ║
  ║  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   ║
  ║                                                                       ║
  ║  Real-world use: Spring Boot uses this pattern.                       ║
  ║  Your pom.xml → <parent>spring-boot-starter-parent → inherits ALL    ║
  ║  Spring managed version properties automatically.                     ║
  ╚═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╝
================================================================================
SECTION 14: PACKAGE ORGANIZATION — ROLE OF EACH PACKAGE EXPLAINED
================================================================================
  Package Name          Role / Responsibility
  ────────────────────  ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  in.ineuron            Root package — main class lives here
  in.ineuron.comp       Component layer — business beans, DAO implementations
  in.ineuron.dependent  Dependency layer — interfaces + their implementations
  in.ineuron.persist    Persistence config — @Configuration classes for DataSource
  in.ineuron.dto        Data Transfer Objects — plain POJO representations of data
  in.ineuron.cfg        Legacy XML config files (applicationContext.xml)
  in.pwskills           Root for Maven/Hibernate standalone projects
  in.pwskills.model     Entity/Model layer — @Entity classes mapped to DB tables
  in.pwskills.util      Utility classes — HibernateUtil (SessionFactory Singleton)
  LAYERED ARCHITECTURE (for Spring projects):
  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │  Presentation / Entry Layer: main() + App     │ ← in.ineuron.Boot...Application
  ├──────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │  Business Component Layer: @Component, @Repo  │ ← in.ineuron.comp
  ├──────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │  Contract (Interface) Layer                   │ ← in.ineuron.dependent
  ├──────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │  Configuration Layer: @Configuration, @Bean   │ ← in.ineuron.persist
  ├──────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │  Data Model Layer: DTOs / Entities            │ ← in.ineuron.dto
  ├──────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │  Database Layer: MySQL / Oracle               │ ← actual DB
  └──────────────────────────────────────────────┘
